Negotiations on Various War Zone Issues Temporarily Stalled

(Beiping) Various issues related to the cleanup of the war zone, such as the Yutian militia dispute and the takeover of the Eastern Tombs and Malanyu, have been negotiated since the establishment of the War Zone Cleanup Committee. Recently, due to the Chahar incident, they have been shelved again. Authorities have stated that they will continue to negotiate a resolution in accordance with the established principles. (29th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Liu Zuozhou, the commander of the 1st Security Brigade in the Luan County war zone, unified the entire county's civil defense, expanded his strength, and organized the civil defense into nine districts, transforming the scattered into the organized, stationed in major towns. He also ordered each village to pay monthly salaries and horse feed for more than three civil defense members. Gentry from Luan County jointly telegraphed the province, requesting an order to stop it. (29th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) About 170 remnant bandits from Liu Guitang's band sneaked into Tuxianzhuang village in the 4th district of Yutian on the evening of the 26th, kidnapped men and women. On the morning of the 27th, the civil defense unit led by Wang Chengzhu and the unit led by Fei Zhuoru rushed to encircle and suppress them. The bandits occupied the east and west entrances of the village, using sandbags to build trenches and possessing handheld machine guns and other weapons to resist the militia. Fierce fighting has been going on for two days. As of the night of the 28th, the militia was still besieging the village. The bandits occupied the village, which is surrounded by water on three sides, giving them an advantage, causing many casualties to the militia. (29th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Qian'an telephone: More than 200 bandits, armed with complete firearms and wearing very neat uniforms, sneaked into the vicinity of Santunying in Xifengkou on the 27th, causing serious disturbances in the area. Due to strength issues, the militia and police have retreated. They have begun to transfer dispersed militia from various villages to the vicinity of Santunying to encircle and suppress them. It is reported that most of the bandits are remnants of the Poor People's Society. Weizhuang in Xinjizhen, Qian'an County, was suddenly attacked by more than 60 bandits on the night of the 26th of this month. After being discovered by the village militia, they immediately opened fire. After an hour of fierce fighting between the two sides, the bandits fled from Doushankou. (29th Dispatch)

Sun and Wang Arrive in Nanjing Together

(Nanjing) Sun Ke and Wang Longhui arrived in Nanjing together on the morning of the 29th. Wang will stay in Nanjing for several days to visit relevant central authorities and continue to discuss the issue of unity. Wang said that he met with Li Xiaosheng, who came north from Hong Kong, and Liu Luyin in Shanghai. Li's arrival was at his invitation to inquire about the recent situation in Guangdong Province, so the meeting with Li was a verbal conversation. Li did not bring any letters from Hu. Li is staying in Shanghai to handle private matters and does not plan to come to Nanjing. As for the issue of unity, he very much hopes to have concrete results before going abroad to resume his duties. The current situation of discussions from all sides shows that it is urgently necessary to consolidate the central authorities. Hu's expressions are also extremely willing to concentrate efforts, and personal whereabouts have not been considered. Therefore, Hu has no preparations to leave Hong Kong at present. Judging from the current progress, the concrete methods of unity are only a matter of time. He is scheduled to go abroad within February, so the time he stays in Nanjing and Shanghai is about one month. Whether he will pass through Hong Kong again to meet Hu when going abroad is currently undecided, but if he takes an Italian mail ship, then Hong Kong is a necessary stop. At that time, he may consider going ashore for a conversation. (29th Dispatch)

Military Ministry Revises Army Leave Rules

(Nanjing) The Military Ministry has revised the Army Leave Rules. Soldiers who are more than seven days overdue will be punished with labor service; those who are more than seven days overdue will be punished with confinement. Officers who are more than 30 days overdue will be suspended from duty. There are only three days of leave throughout the year: January 1st, March 29th, and November 12th. (29th Dispatch)

Yu Jishi Telegraphs Capture of Bandit Leader Fang Zhimin

Many People Captured Near Huaiyushan; Zhao Guantao Dispatches Personnel to Escort to Shangrao

(Hangzhou) Yu Jishi telegraphed the province tonight, stating that at 7:30 this morning, they jointly attacked Huaiyushan. The bandits were trapped for ten days, hungry and cold. Fang Zhimin only led four bandits down the mountain in a disheveled state, attempting to escape between Chenjiawan and Nuanshui near Huaiyushan, and were captured alive by our army. In addition, important bandit leaders, such as Li Shubin, Director of the Political Department of the Pseudo 19th Division, and Tan Boqing, Minister of Health, were captured with more than ten light and heavy machine guns, countless radios and military supplies in the vicinity of the mountain. At 6 p.m., Fang and Liu had been escorted by Zhao Guantao to the Shangrao Four Province Border Garrison Headquarters for interrogation. (29th Dispatch)

(Hangzhou) The Security Office received a telegram from Yu Jishi from Changshan stating that Liu Zhouxi, the regiment commander of Chi Bandit Fang Zhimin's pseudo 10th Army, was captured today in Chenjiawan, east of Nuanshui, northwest of Huaiyushan. Fang only led six or seven people, hiding in Huaiyushan. According to Fang, he is the Chairman of the Southeast Military Committee, and Liu is a member. Their troops are called the Northward Anti-Japanese Vanguard. (29th Dispatch)

Jiang Bandits Gather in Xinfeng and Attack Niuling, Repelled

(Hong Kong) About 3,000 remnant Jiang bandits of the pseudo 7th Division recently gathered in Xiaoxi area of Xinfeng, attacking Niuling. Huang Zhinan, Deputy Division Commander of the Guangdong 2nd Division, led two regiments to suppress them on the 27th, and after five hours of fighting, repelled the bandits south of Niuling, seizing more than 200 guns. A portion of the bandits are resisting on the high ground northwest of Niuling. (29th Dispatch)

League of Nations Experts Inspect Water Conservancy Situation

(Jinan) A group of League of Nations experts inspected the old canal lock at Shilibu this morning, then came east to Taochengbu, crossed the river to the north bank, which is the site of the Changyuan breach, where water enters the main stream of the Yellow River. After inspecting, they went west along the river to see the situation of the north bank levee, arrived at Zhangqiu Town, paid tribute to Wu Jizha's sword-hanging site, and returned to Taochengbu to see the old canal lock. The canal can directly connect to Tianjin. The Construction Office has completed the repair of the riverbed and is preparing to dredge the water for navigation. After viewing, they came east. Militia from various counties along the way added guards. They arrived at Guanzhuang at noon to see the dangerous works, and at Hongmiao in Qihe at three o'clock to see the siphon irrigation, and at Luokou at four o'clock. They crossed the river to Ji'nan, and are scheduled to visit Han on the 30th for a banquet, and will inspect the lower reaches of the Yellow River and the Xiaoqing River again on the 31st. Active Export of Horticultural Products

(Nanjing) According to the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute, the export of horticultural products in our country is relatively active. According to customs statistics, between 1927 and 1931, the average export value of oranges and other categories was 9,770,052 customs taels, and the export of rapeseed and other categories was 19,204,261 customs taels. However, backward production technology, improper packaging methods, and inaccurate grading all pose a risk of products being rejected in foreign markets. It is hoped that domestic horticulturists will pay attention to improvements. (29th Central News Agency Dispatch)

China's Reply is About to be Sent

Ariyoshi's Visit to Nanjing to Meet Wang is a Routine Visit, Not a Mission

(Nanjing) Japanese Ambassador Ariyoshi, accompanied by Counselor Ariye, Secretary Horiuchi, and Clerk Yokokawa, arrived in Nanjing at 7:00 AM on the 29th via the Shanghai-Nanjing overnight express train, with a reserved carriage. Suma, the Japanese Consul-General in Nanjing, along with consulate staff, welcomed them at Xiaguan Station. After a brief exchange of greetings, Ariyoshi and his entourage left the station and proceeded by car to the Japanese Consulate-General for rest. According to Ariye, speaking to reporters at the station, Ambassador Ariyoshi routinely visits Nanjing every month or two to call on the Chinese Foreign Ministry. This visit is a routine one and does not involve any specific mission. The ambassador is scheduled to call on President Wang at 5:00 PM on the 29th and plans to visit Chairman Chiang on the 30th, but the time has not yet been confirmed. The ambassador is expected to return to Shanghai on the overnight express train on the evening of the 30th. He also mentioned that the situation in Eastern Chahar, according to recent reports from the embassy, has calmed down again, and both sides are discussing solutions. This is a local matter being handled by the Kwantung Army and the Hebei authorities. Rumors that the ambassador will soon return to Japan are inaccurate. (Central News Agency dispatch, 29th)

(Nanjing) Japanese Ambassador Ariyoshi, accompanied by Ariye, visited President Wang at the Tiebu official residence at 4:30 PM on the 29th. Gao Zongwu, assistant of the Asian Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, was also present. They talked for about an hour. At 5:50 PM, Ariyoshi and his party departed. Wang hosted a banquet for Ariyoshi at 8:00 PM, with Tang Youren and others in attendance. It is reported that Ariyoshi mentioned to Wang during their meeting on the 29th, in addition to routine greetings, that anti-Japanese actions still exist in various parts of China and hoped that the Chinese government would pay attention. Finally, they discussed the Eastern Chahar incident, which he said would not escalate and could likely be resolved locally. (Central News Agency dispatch, 29th)

(Nanjing) Japanese Ambassador Ariyoshi, accompanied by Counselor Ariye, Secretary Horiuchi, and Clerk Yokokawa, this morning, the 29th. At approximately 4:00 PM, Ariyoshi and Ariye visited President Wang at Tiebu No. 1 Official Residence. Gao Zongwu, assistant of the Asian Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, was also present. Ariyoshi raised the issue of anti-Japanese actions in various parts of China, according to reports received by the Japanese Embassy, and hoped that the Chinese government would pay attention to it. Ariyoshi then stated that he believed the Eastern Chahar issue would not escalate and could be resolved locally. The discussion concluded at 5:50 PM. At 8:00 PM in the evening, Wang hosted a banquet for Ariyoshi at the official residence, with Minister of Interior Huang Fu and both Vice Ministers and Directors of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in attendance. Ariyoshi is scheduled to take the train to Shanghai on the evening of the 30th. (Special Dispatch, 29th)

Current Commentary

A Review of the Review of Sino-Japanese Relations

— Zhen

China and Japan are geographically so close, and their economic relations so intertwined. Yet, since the September 18th Incident (Mukden Incident), their emotional ties have been broken, and they have been deadlocked to this day. As Xu Daolin said in his article "Enemy or Friend," "...they are heading further down a dead end." Whether the Japanese authorities will deeply reflect upon and sincerely improve relations between the two countries after Xu's review is unknown. However, informed individuals in that country should be able to make further assessments to break the Sino-Japanese deadlock. As for the attitude of our Chinese people toward Japan, we should look inward at ourselves and outward at the overall situation, making a very serious evaluation and consideration, and not continue to view Japan with animosity.

In the section where Xu explains "the advantages and disadvantages of prolonging the deadlock from China's perspective," he first quotes Sun Yat-sen's teachings, stating that China and Japan benefit from cooperation and suffer from conflict. This is especially evident during the recent surge in economic development alliances promoting nationalistic economies. If relations deteriorate to the end, our country will make unprecedented sacrifices to seek a glimmer of hope amidst certain death. The harm suffered by Japan, compared to ours, will likely exceed ours. Therefore, we hope that our countrymen will study Xu's article in depth, and especially that the Japanese side will carefully consider it, to find a way to break the deadlock. The talk of a second world war has been going on for a long time. Currently, it is restricted by economic conditions from breaking out immediately, but it will inevitably happen in the future. How should our country handle itself then? This is currently the most serious issue. All those who deeply understand international relations and the Far Eastern situation are concerned about this for our country. Xu said emphatically, "Maintaining neutrality..." is no different from a fool's dream..." His active proposal is "The only viable path... is to do everything possible to eliminate the chance of war..." and "...the Sino-Japanese issue, which is one of the causes of war, must be resolved..." These are wise words.

However, we believe that until the Sino-Japanese issue is resolved, the past cannot be thoroughly cleared up. Not only will Japan face tremendous obstacles, leading to complications and increasing future worries, but our country's intention for peace will also easily lead to misunderstandings from the Japanese side, even causing unfortunate results. This is because some of the "China experts" in Japan often have factual errors in their understanding in the positive aspect. For example, they have consistently lacked a full understanding of the progress of the Chinese revolution in the past, making malicious speculations, which has led to an irreconcilable conflict. Regarding national relations, they try their best to seek out China's shortcomings from the dark side, while having little understanding of the strengths and goodwill of the Chinese nation. Therefore, it is difficult for the people of both countries to find a path to sincere understanding. Since the September 18th Incident, Japan has often subjected our country to unbearable humiliations, spreading the seeds of animosity between nations. If this continues, it will likely fall into an irretrievable situation. Xu described this kind of evil cause in great detail. This is what the Japanese side should first be aware of.

Recently, the entire world political situation, such as the easing of Franco-German opposition, the establishment of understanding between France and Italy, and the United States joining the International Court of Justice, all show signs of peace and reduce the floating war clouds. How the Far Eastern relations will develop is also up to human effort. If Japan is truly sincere in abandoning hatred and seeking friendship, and changes its past intentions, then the premise should be, as Xu said, first, "Abandon territorial aggression and return the four northeastern provinces!" Second, establish mutually beneficial relations based on the principle of equality of national interests. If these principles can be followed in order, then all outstanding issues between China and Japan can be resolved gradually, and there might be a glimmer of hope for breaking the current deadlock.

Molotov, Chairman of the Soviet Union, Speaks on International Relations

Denies Intention to Invade Xinjiang in China; Defenses are Secure, Not Afraid of Japan; Relations with Germany are Extremely Bad

(Moscow) Molotov, Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union, today delivered a speech at the opening session of the Seventh Congress of Soviets, criticizing foreign criticism of the recent Soviet execution of political prisoners, saying that the Soviet government will continue to apply the same punishment to all enemies. Molotov also said that relations between the Soviet Union and China are very good and denied foreign reports that the Soviet Union intends to control Xinjiang. Molotov believed that some Japanese militarists particularly desire war, but the Soviet Union has strengthened its defenses and is fully prepared to deal with it. Relations with Germany, however, are extremely bad because Germany has plans to invade Soviet territory. Molotov further stated that the disarmament conference has completely failed, but the Soviet Union still hopes that it can create a permanent organization against war in the graveyard of Geneva. Molotov's speech focused on the economic progress of the Soviet Union, saying that since 1929, industrial output has risen by 139%, while the capitalist world outside the Soviet Union has declined by 24%. The Soviet Union's financial situation has also greatly improved since the last Congress of Soviets in 1931. Most importantly, cash income has increased sixfold, and foreign debt has decreased by three-quarters. Finally, Molotov again discussed the possibility of war in the Far East, saying that the number of Red Army soldiers has increased, and its mechanization has also greatly improved. (National News Agency, 28th)

(Moscow) The All-Union Congress of Soviets opened here today, with a total of 2,000 representatives from all departments across the country attending. Molotov, Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars and Chairman of the Council of Labor and Defense, gave a passionate speech to the audience, strongly arguing that the Soviet Union's military strength should continue to be expanded. Molotov said that in the past four years, the mechanization of the Soviet Army has been four times higher than before. The Soviet Army now has more artillery batteries, tanks, and aircraft, and the defense projects in the East are more solid than before. However, Molotov acknowledged that the First Five-Year Plan was not fully implemented due to the surge in defense spending, which was not anticipated. Several representatives attending the meeting traveled hundreds of miles through icy and snowy lands on sledges pulled by reindeer. Stalin was warmly welcomed by the representatives when he entered the venue, and the cheers lasted for more than five minutes. Molotov continued, "We must consider that the danger of war against Russia is now greater than before. Responsible parties in Japan have long openly discussed war against Russia, and we must not forget that there are new parties in power in Europe who openly declare that occupying Soviet territory is their historical mission. Since the rise of the German National Socialist Party, no one can turn a blind eye to the changes in Russian-German relations." Molotov then mentioned Hitler's book "Mein Kampf" and asked the audience, "Are Hitler's remarks about the necessity of territorial aggression in Eastern Europe still valid today? When the National Socialist Party speaks of new territories in Europe, are they still thinking of Russia and its neighbors?" Molotov continued that Hitler's words are clearly still valid because, apart from Germany's attitude toward the Eastern European treaties, many events in Russian-German relations can only be understood with reference to this issue. Molotov concluded, "We must decide our own views." (Reuters, 28th)

(Moscow) When Molotov spoke, he commented on the relations between the Soviet Union and China, saying, "Sino-Soviet relations, which were damaged after the oppression of Soviet elements in China in 1928, have now been restored. The Chinese government clearly believes that the break in relations was not only not beneficial to China but also made its international position worse. Some people may need this kind of practical and objective lesson, but that is their own business and does not concern us. We knew at that time (as we do now) that correct Sino-Soviet relations are beneficial to both countries and to world peace. Therefore, when the Chinese government proposed the resumption of relations with the Soviet Union, we gladly accepted, so that our country can consolidate friendship with the great Chinese people. I would like to briefly address the malicious rumors of the 'Sovietization' of Xinjiang again. These anti-Soviet rumors were clearly created by Japan, and Japan's policy towards China is already known to everyone and cannot be concealed by spreading rumors. I must solemnly point out that the Soviet Union's actual policy towards China, the policy of seizing foreign territory, is not suitable for the Soviet Union. The Soviet Union unconditionally supports the independence and inviolability of all parts of China (including Xinjiang)." (TASS, 29th)

Japanese House of Representatives Questions Military Spending Issues

Ogawa Says Internal and External Atmosphere is Uneasy

(Tokyo) The confrontational state between the government and the Seiyukai party in the House of Representatives budget committee remains unchanged. Today's meeting began with Ogawa Gotaro questioning national defense finance issues.

Ogawa asked, "Today's situation is extraordinarily serious. The internal and external atmosphere is uneasy. Eliminating this uneasy atmosphere is a political matter. Therefore, the cabinet's policies must be clearly defined. Is there a distinction in importance between the government's ten major policy plans, establishing finance and protecting national defense? What is the Prime Minister's view on this?"

Prime Minister Okada replied, "There is no distinction in importance between national defense security and the establishment of finance."

Minister of the Army Hayashi and Minister of the Navy Osumi also gave the same response.

Ogawa further asked, "It is heard that the Ministers of the Army and Navy acknowledged the coordination of national defense and economic power at the previous cabinet meeting. Is this true? What are Foreign Minister Hirota's observations regarding the outcome of the disarmament conference? According to the Foreign Minister's statements, war will not occur. Then, will naval military spending be reduced because of this?"

Foreign Minister Hirota replied, "My belief is that war will not occur. There has been no change in this so far. If the disarmament conference is successful, then naval military spending should be reduced."

Ogawa asked, "The so-called 'war will not occur,' does that mean you have hope for the disarmament conference? Then, can the Foreign Minister's true intention be interpreted as the result of disarmament will allow for thorough savings in naval military spending in the future?"

The Foreign Minister replied, "I hope that the disarmament agreement will be established. If it can be established, it will be possible to thoroughly save naval military spending. Therefore, I hope that the people will work together to promote the disarmament conference."

Ogawa asked, "What are the Navy Minister's observations regarding the above issue?"

Navy Minister Osumi replied, "If the disarmament conference can be established, it would be best. We are working hard under this policy."

Ogawa asked, "If the disarmament conference breaks down, will a naval arms race occur? The general public is anxious about this, which gives the financial world anxiety. We would like to hear the government's opinion on this."

Navy Minister Osumi's response was the same as what he said in the Diet last time and will not be repeated here.

Ogawa asked, "If the disarmament conference breaks down, it is said that the people must have extraordinary determination. What does this statement mean? Please explain."

Navy Minister Osumi replied, "As the disarmament conference is not yet clear today, it is not appropriate to talk about situations that could cause misunderstandings. Countries today all hope not to increase the burden on their people, and there is concern that an unfortunate military expansion competition will occur in the future. If we want to take it further and make various predictions, I feel it is inappropriate to discuss. I believe that even if the disarmament conference breaks down, we can continue to support it with the current military spending, and the situation will not be much different. I have the belief that we can support it."

The questioning ended here, and a recess was announced. It was 0:10 AM. It was originally planned to continue the budget committee meeting in the afternoon, but due to the time constraints of the main session, the meeting was adjourned. (Japan Associated Press, 29th)

(London) The Times published an article written by Sir Cecil Clementi, former Governor of the British Straits Settlements, arguing that the British Embassy in China should not be located in Beijing. His reasons were that "It is now easy for Europeans to understand that Beijing is isolated from the trends of Chinese people's lives. It is not the true capital of China. In the past, northern peoples invaded the Central Plains and established their capital here to control the eighteen provinces. Now, the Chinese government has established its capital in Nanjing. For the sake of a good understanding between Europe and China, Europeans should eliminate the illusion that Beijing represents a unified China. If its people were to choose their own capital, it would definitely not be Beijing. All those who are familiar with the facts of China should deeply believe this. As Beijing is now merely a city government located in a remote corner of China, it is not appropriate for foreign diplomatic representatives to be stationed in Beijing. However, given the current situation in Beijing, it is quite difficult to choose another suitable place for foreign envoys to reside. The purpose of British merchants is to engage in peaceful and prosperous trade with all parts of China, and the task of British diplomatic envoys is to maintain friendly relations with the de facto authorities in the eighteen provinces of China. Therefore, in my personal opinion, the British Embassy should be temporarily located in Shanghai, as Shanghai is a transportation hub and is very close to Nanjing. It is more convenient for the British Ambassador to reside in Shanghai permanently and travel to various parts of China at any time." (Havas, 29th)

British House of Commons Debates Supplementary Budget

Disturbance Occurs in Solemn Chamber

Labor MP Scorns Prime Minister as Fox Spirit

Spectators Shout "Down with the Government" in Response

Sixty Demonstrators Expelled from Chamber

(London) Last night, when the House of Commons debated a supplementary budget of £5 million to fund the new Unemployment Assistance Board, a great disturbance occurred in the spectator gallery. First, Labour MP Buchanan spoke, defaming Prime Minister MacDonald, calling him a "fox spirit," "pig," "scoundrel," and "villain," and saying he should be whipped with a riding crop and banished from public life. The MPs were astonished to hear this. Then, women in the spectator gallery stood up and shouted, "Down with the National Government," "Down with those who starve babies." Just as the demonstrators were being escorted out of the House by the police, others stood up and continued the demonstration. The chaos was indescribable and lasted for several minutes. A total of sixty people were expelled. Then, Speaker FitzRoy ordered all those in the spectator gallery to leave the House, and they left reluctantly. The House then resumed its discussion. Before Buchanan insulted the government, the government's proposals to relieve unemployment had been warmly condemned. The Unemployment Assistance Board has now been ordered to standardize the regulations for relief to healthy unemployed workers nationwide. Buchanan is one of the most radical Labour MPs in the House. He has been a representative of Glasgow since 1922. He studied at Cowcaddens Public School in Glasgow and later engaged in the labor movement. He was elected as a member of the Glasgow City Council in 1918 and is now 54 years old. Today, he was referred to as a "hero" by those in the spectator gallery. Prime Minister MacDonald did not attend the House of Commons today and therefore did not personally hear Buchanan's attack. (Reuters, 29th)

This Session's Agenda

(London) The reopening of the British Parliament this time resembles the eve of a general election. The agenda for this session includes numerous proposals. The government has submitted seven bills, the most important of which are the Indian New Constitution Bill and the Unemployment Extra Relief Fund Bill. The Cabinet predicts that the next budget will be a "prosperity budget." If the financial economy truly enters a prosperous period, then all of the Labor Party's accusations can be fundamentally eliminated. If, by the end of this parliamentary session, the financial situation and the "Poverty Class Relief Committee" established by the government both achieve satisfactory results, the government will hold a general election in October of this year to gain the people's trust. If, by that time, the government's various measures have not yielded results, then the general election will be postponed to February 1936. In addition, there are various other issues that are sufficient to affect the political situation and make it uncertain. The first is the government's foreign policy. The British government's attitude towards the arms issue and various international conventions is attracting great attention from public opinion. Before French Prime Minister Flandin and Foreign Minister Laval come to London, several questions have already been listed on the parliamentary agenda, awaiting Foreign Minister Simon's response. The second is the return of the Liberal Party elder and former Prime Minister Lloyd George to the political stage. Lloyd George has recently been giving speeches everywhere, attacking the government and vigorously advocating for a controlled economy. Even if this move does not endanger the position and reputation of the National Government, it will at least provide a strong stimulus to the current government. (Havas News Agency, 28th)

Protecting Marine Territories, US Organizes Air Force Headquarters

Commanding the Air Force to Deal with Contingencies, Wake Island to Be Developed as a Air Station

(Washington) Army officials and senior officers are all eager for the newly organized Air Force Headquarters to protect America's marine territories. Chief of Staff McArthur declared today that after the establishment of the new organizational law, the national air defense's activity will be much different than in the past. McArthur also said, "I plan to use the Air Force to deal with all contingencies when necessary, whether it is in Panama, Hawaii, or the Philippines, all can be done. A powerful Air Force can reach the Philippines via Hawaii and Guam. In short, I will send the Air Force to any location when necessary." According to the new plan, the US Air Force will maintain full strength at all times, unlike the infantry, cavalry, and artillery, which are reduced to very small numbers in peacetime. In the event that the enemy breaks through the US Navy and lands on the mainland or any marine territory, the new air defense plan will immediately dispatch the Air Force to prevent the enemy from expanding the occupied area, pending the arrival of the Army to engage in battle. Army aviation experts are now studying how to fly to the Philippines via the US-owned islands in the Pacific. The first step may be to use Wake Island, which is 2,200 miles west of Hawaii and 2,600 miles east of the Philippines, as a base for seaplanes. Recently, Navy Secretary Swanson said that the project of developing Wake Island as a commercial aviation field in the Pacific is under consideration. According to the plan of the Air Force Headquarters, five military stations will also be established on the US mainland, each with 200 aircraft permanently stationed, but ready to fly to threatened locations at any time. (National News Agency, 28th)

What Do Japanese Naval Minister's Remarks Refer To? Generally Believed to Be Aimed at Russia

Officials here heard this and did not know what he was referring to. If no other country initiates it, the United States has no intention of engaging in naval competition. The current US Navy is still 78 ships short of the treaty limit, and the Navy Secretary's request to add only 14 ships will not allow the US Navy to reach the treaty limit until 1942. Saar Transfer Issue, France and Germany Discuss Details

(Basel) Representatives of German and French experts, members of the Saar Governing Commission, and representatives of the League of Nations' Three-Member Committee held a second meeting here today to discuss various details related to the Saar transfer issue. US and Russia Joining the Governing Body Creates Difficulties for the ILO

No Vacancies in the Current Eight Seats, Committee Studies New Methods

(Geneva) The League of Nations' International Labor Organization Governing Body met here today, and the accession of the United States and Soviet Russia has created difficulties. According to the Treaty of Versailles, only representatives of the eight major industrial countries can serve as permanent directors. The so-called eight major industrial countries are Belgium, Canada, France, Germany, the United Kingdom, India, Italy, and Japan. If the US and Russia join the ILO, they must each occupy a permanent seat, and at present it is not easy to obtain two vacancies. Although Japan has announced its withdrawal from the League of Nations, it still retains its membership in the ILO. Germany's seat must also be left vacant, as Germany may return to the League of Nations. Therefore, it is quite difficult and cannot be resolved without a voting method. If two permanent seats must be added, it will take several years of twists and turns. The ILO has now formed a committee of experts to study a new method so that two of the eight countries' representatives can give up their permanent seats. However, this report must wait for the next meeting to be discussed, and it is still questionable whether a solution can be found, so the results may have to be referred to the League of Nations Administrative Council. In addition, there is another difficulty, which is how Soviet Russia can comply with the regulations and send representatives from both labor and capital to attend the ILO. (National News Agency, 29th)

Turkish Windstorm Uproots Trees, Collapses Houses, Disrupts Traffic

(Istanbul, Turkey) A major and minor windstorm occurred here, causing railway traffic to be disrupted for several days. Many houses and trees were destroyed by the wind, and the power plant could not generate electricity. At the same time, the city of Smyrna was also hit by a windstorm, houses collapsed, and major and minor fires broke out, destroying many civilian houses, shops, and Jewish churches. The Future of the Japan-Manchukuo Economic Conference

(Japanese Dispatch)

Zaibatsu and Military Clash in the Dark

Financial Contradictions Gradually Exposed

Military Preparations Turning More Active

The disharmony between the civilian government faction and the military in Japan is an open secret that need not be concealed. However, Japan is ultimately a country ruled by law, and its political institutions all have a set framework. Therefore, no matter how powerful the military is, it cannot overstep the boundaries and disregard national law. Since the September 18th Incident, Japanese soldiers have achieved great feats, while the political parties have made no achievements, and cases of embezzlement and bribery have repeatedly emerged. For example, the Teikoku Rayon Company case involved several cabinet members from the Saito Cabinet era. These individuals, including Mitsui, Nakajima, and others, had close ties with the Seiyukai party. As a result, the military became increasingly assertive, and public opinion favored the military and looked down on the political parties. Parliamentary politics existed only in name.

Young military officers (from major to colonel) combined with various patriotic organizations to advocate for the "Restoration of the Imperial Country, Showa Restoration," externally expanding the continental policy and proclaiming the Asia Monroe Doctrine, and internally advocating for national defense and opposing the control of the political situation by financial capital. In rural areas, they promoted land policies, even advocating for returning land to the Emperor and redistributing it. In urban areas, they focused on small and medium-sized industrial and commercial businesses and opposed the monopolistic interests of financial capital. The established political parties, the Seiyukai and the Minseito, all had large financial capital as their backing and supported their monopolistic interests. Therefore, most military officers from small and medium-sized industrial and commercial backgrounds and rural areas were anti-political party and supported various right-leaning patriotic organizations to oppose the political parties. Thus, at the beginning of the establishment of Manchukuo, the military hardliners (i.e., young military officers) had a huge conflict with the local Japanese zaibatsu. The reflection of this in upper-level politics was the open and covert strife between the military headquarters, the embassy, and the governor of the Kwantung Leased Territory in "Manchuria." In Japan, the army ministry, the foreign ministry, and the colonial ministry each acted on its own. It was not until Hirota became foreign minister that the relationship between the army and the foreign ministry gradually improved, while the colonial bureaucrats and the army remained at odds. From the Saito cabinet until November of last year, this kind of dispute did not ease. Unexpectedly, the military used its special powers to set up a special agency in Dalian to implement strong control, and the bureaucrats had to retreat in order to preserve some of their power. Initially, they wanted to divide the interests with the military equally along the South Manchurian Railway line and in the other four northeastern provinces. Later, given the power of the military, they planned to retain the last vestige of colonial control over the Kwantung Leased Territory (Liaodong Peninsula). After the establishment of the Dalian Special Agency, international commercial telecommunications

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today's gold price is 141 shillings and 8.5 pence, up 2.5 pence.

London Silver Bar: In today's silver market, the United States bought, India sold, and speculators engaged in both buying and selling. The market closed steadily with no price movement. Spot price remains at 24.75 pence, futures at 24.875 pence.

Mount Lyell Silver: At the opening of today's silver market, some contract prices remained unchanged, while others rose slightly.

Exchange Rates

Sterling-Dollar: The London foreign exchange market was stable this morning with decent trading. The sterling-dollar exchange rate opened at $4.85875, 0.25 lower than yesterday's closing rate. There was a previous upward trend, and the latest price is $4.8725, up 1.375 from the opening.

Sterling-Franc: In the sterling-franc exchange market, the authorities were not seen using the equalization fund to adjust prices today. The opening price was 74.59 francs, down 6 pounds from yesterday. It fell to 74.46 francs at 2:00 PM, 13 pounds lower than the opening.

Dollar-Sterling: Although the foreign exchange situation has improved, the uncertain situation still has an adverse impact on the market. In this morning's foreign exchange market, the US dollar rose sharply. The sterling exchange rate opened at $4.87625, 1.5 higher than the sterling-dollar closing. The franc exchange rate was $6.545, 2.5 higher than yesterday's closing.

Cotton and Wheat

New York Cotton: The New York cotton market initially saw long positions liquidated, then sentiment turned firm, and later stabilized.

New York Wheat: Wheat supply seems to have decreased significantly, and the liquidation of long positions seems to be over. However, the Chicago wheat market opened slightly lower, and sentiment remained uncertain due to the upcoming verdict on the gold bill.

Liverpool Wheat: In today's wheat market, the May contract price was 5 shillings and 0.5 pence at 1:00 PM, down 0.5 pence.

Liverpool Cotton: In today's cotton market, the May contract price was 6.74 at 1:00 PM, down 1 pound.

Rubber

London: The market opened steadily today, turning lackluster at noon. The transaction price for the April and June contracts was 6.3125 pence, the same as yesterday's closing price.

New York: The New York rubber market showed slight weakness today, and trading was also light.

The unfavorable factors for the market are: labor unrest and uncertainty about the gold bill. The securities market opened lightly and steadily this morning, with limited gains and losses in various securities. Good business news was overshadowed by uncertain situations, and trading is expected to remain difficult to develop. The New York securities market prices are listed below:

The colonial bureaucrats no longer dare to take any action. Even the major capitalists, such as the Mitsui, Mitsubishi, and Furukawa zaibatsu, are unwilling to lightly invest in the Northeast, fearing that if things change, their assets and businesses will be wiped out.

The original intention of the zaibatsu was to hope that the military could gradually comply and completely obey the instructions of financial capital, and to constantly use parliamentary politics to restore the so-called constitutional normalcy and form a political dictatorship of financial capital. All rights in "Manchuria" must be controlled by the zaibatsu, or at least they should have the right to intervene. Unexpectedly, the military's behavior was completely the opposite. It was impossible to obey the zaibatsu, and even equal consultation required serious instructions from the military, resembling an appendage. This situation is obvious to all.

Recently, in the so-called Japan-Manchukuo Economic Conference, the zaibatsu believed that the economic trends in Japan this year mostly showed signs of deterioration. For example, the excessive issuance of government bonds was likely to cause vicious inflation. Various countries, such as the United Kingdom and the United States, were trying to control their own markets, and it was difficult to further develop the export of light industrial products. Therefore, they planned to seize a large number of economic benefits in the Northeast to compensate for the lack of foreign exports. However, the Japanese military's intention was completely the opposite. The so-called Japan-Manchukuo economic cooperation placed the highest priority on Japan's national defense. Therefore, joint ventures were mainly special companies. Second, the conference location was in Changchun. Third, the four Japanese committee members were the Chief of Staff of the Kwantung Army, the Counselor of the Embassy, the Director-General of the Kwantung Bureau, and representatives appointed by the Bureau of Manchurian Affairs. They formed a joint organization with an equal number of people from the Manchukuo side. Japanese capitalists were not allowed to participate, and even offering opinions was not allowed. Initially, what they had hoped for was: 1) the conference in Tokyo; 2) at least two representatives from the zaibatsu participating; 3) mainly benefiting the Japanese financial community. Now that the conference has been fully revealed, the zaibatsu's expectations have been dashed. They expressed dissatisfaction with the Japan-Manchukuo Economic Conference, believing that it would hinder the prospect of investment and have a very bad impact on the Japanese economic community. The Economic Conference not only looked down on the zaibatsu and did not allow them to participate, but its organization was also completely controlled by the Kwantung Army and was merely a special agency of the Kwantung Army. As a result, the dark strife between the military and the zaibatsu will turn into open struggle. Recent trends suggest that victory may ultimately go to the military. (January 24, Tokyo)

Eastern Chahar After the Japanese Bombing

Japanese Troops Suddenly Increase and Decrease, Intentions Unclear

Wounded Soldiers and Civilians Have Been Sent to Zhangjiakou for Treatment

Negotiation Location Still Under Discussion

Beiping Correspondence: Regarding the Chahar East issue, both sides are seeking a peaceful solution. However, the Japanese and puppet troops have been continuously increasing their forces and transferring them in various parts of Chahar East in recent days. According to a phone call from Zhangjiakou this morning (27th), Japanese troops in Changliang, Xifengzhai, North and South Shizhuzi, and Datan suddenly increased and decreased their forces, with unclear intentions. Aircraft have been scouting Guyuan and Dushikou from time to time, but have not yet dropped bombs. Our troops have not been mobilized at all. A total of 37 soldiers and civilians who were injured by Japanese aircraft bombing in the Dongzhaizi and Dushikou areas were transported to Zhangjiakou for treatment from Dushikou at 6:00 PM on the 25th. According to injured personnel, most of the injured were residents of Guyuan Twenty Mile Fort, Dongzhaizi, and Dushikou. When Japanese aircraft dropped bombs, they flew at extremely low altitudes, only three or four zhang away from the houses, so the bombing was exceptionally accurate. The original 40-odd households in Dongzhaizi have now been completely evacuated, except for the injured. All houses have been destroyed by aircraft and artillery fire, turning into a scorched earth, which is extremely miserable. Only government agencies such as the county government, public security bureau, and court, and a few households of residents remain in Guyuan City. Districts 2 and 4 were occupied by Japanese and puppet troops long ago. Outside Dushikou, there are no formal troops stationed on our side. Japanese and puppet troops have advanced to Xifengzhai and Wuni, approaching the Great Wall line, and increasing troops in those areas. According to people from Yanqing, Japanese and puppet troops sent personnel to the Sihai area of the county a few days ago, forcibly designating the area as a puppet state territory and demanding that households pay taxes. The local people are still very calm.

Regarding negotiation information, the Japanese representatives Matsui and Takahashi cannot make decisions on their own. The Japanese side proposes that the negotiation location be in Chengde, Datan, Gubeikou, or Shanhaiguan, while our side believes that it would be more convenient to be in Beiping or Tianjin. Matsui and Takahashi have telegraphed the Kwantung Army for instructions. Contact can only begin after a reply. Xiao Zhenying went to Juren Hall again on the morning of the 27th to visit He Yingqin. According to Xiao, the Chahar Province has telegraphed the central government on the continuous situation and the losses caused by Japanese aircraft bombing. All negotiation matters are subject to the central government's orders. (January 27)

Rural Reconstruction Commission Investigates Anhui Province's Rice Industry

Provincial Government Committee Members Supervise Emergency Relief

Wuhu Correspondence: When the collection of relief grain in Anhui Province was suspended, Premier Wang of the Executive Yuan telegraphed Anhui Chairman Liu Zhenhua, saying that the disaster relief after the bandit suppression in southern Anhui would be assisted in other ways, and the Ministry of Finance and the Rural Reconstruction Commission would send personnel to Anhui to investigate in order to seek relief methods. After receiving the order, the Rural Reconstruction Commission sent Secretary Li Jingmi, specialist Lin Xizhao, commissioner Sun Xiaocun, and investigator Liao Fengqin to Anqing to investigate first. Last night, they took a ship from Anqing to Wuhu and met with Yuan Doushu, the representative of the Anhui Province Sail Transportation Rice Industry in Wuhu, and Li Dachu, the chairman of the Transportation Industry Association, to inquire in detail about the recent situation of the rice industry. The Reconstruction Commission's investigation paid special attention to the three aspects of production, transportation, and sales of rice in Anhui Province, intending to analyze and statistically improve the export of Anhui rice. At the same time, the relief grain previously collected in Anhui Province must also be investigated clearly in order to determine the post-disaster relief methods after the relief grain is revoked. Li et al. have reported the details of the rice production and sales investigation in Wuhu to the Reconstruction Commission in order to determine the principles for reconstructing the rural areas of Anhui Province based on the surplus and deficiency of various parts of the country. It is also heard that the investigators will transfer to North China to work after the matters in Wuhu are completed.

Since the establishment of the Relief Grain Collection Office in Anhui Province, it has collected about 100,000 shi of relief rice and stipulated distribution rules. All counties receiving relief grain must appoint commissioners to supervise the implementation of emergency relief agricultural loans and price stabilization together with the county magistrates. If the county magistrate is perfunctory or engages in malfeasance in relief affairs, the committee may report to the provincial government to dismiss or punish him with salary deductions or record demerits. It is now found that there are 39 counties receiving relief grain, including Huaining. However, in order to save travel expenses, it has been decided by the provincial government's quick discussion to assign one supervisory commissioner for every three counties, who will depart immediately to handle matters together with the county, thereby providing relief. (January 26)

Fellow Townsmen from Wuyuan Oppose the Sale of the Nanjing Examination Hall

Beijing News: The Nanjing Wuyuan Examination Hall used to be a place for scholars from the hometown to stay when they came to Beijing for the provincial examination from afar. The building is magnificent and spacious. Since the abolition of the imperial examination system, it has become a convenient place for fellow townsmen traveling abroad. It also has annual rents and other attached market house rents, totaling more than a thousand yuan, which can cover expenses. In recent years, it has been managed by the Wuyuan Education Bureau on behalf of the Wuyuan community, and the surplus is used to subsidize local education. It is not official property. Recently, it has been heard that the Wude Road is lacking funds for construction, and the Wuyuan Temporary Local Clearing and Rehabilitation Committee, Finance Committee, Chamber of Commerce, and Tea Merchants Association are planning to sell the hall to fund the road construction. Fellow townsmen from various places are protesting. The letter from the Wuyuan Fellow Townsmen Association in Changzhou is recorded as follows: "Gentlemen of the four groups, Upon receiving letters from the fellow townsmen associations in Beijing, Shanghai, Wuxi, etc., we have read that you are proposing to sell the Nanjing Wuyuan Examination Hall for road construction expenses due to the urgent need for funds for Wude Road and the difficulty in raising funds among families. It is not impossible to do this in principle. Since the imperial examination system was abolished, there is no need for the existence of an examination hall in its literal sense. However, we remember that the examination hall was established by the wise men of the past, is grand in scale, and benefits the local scholars. It is located in the Gu Lou Kou area. Although transportation is not extremely convenient, in today's rapidly developing capital construction, things are changing every month and day. Who knows that it will not be a bustling city in the future? According to land value, it changes with the prosperity of the market. If Gu Lou Kou becomes a bustling market one day, the value of the examination hall's land alone will be worth at least 100,000. Its accompanying real estate is not without hope. In terms of benefits, it seems appropriate to be patient for a moment and wait for the opportunity. If you are drinking poison to quench your thirst and are too hasty to choose, selling such a promising property at a cheap price, even if the Wuyuan community remains silent, you will feel ashamed to face the wise men of the past. Furthermore, Wude Road is another issue. If fellow townsmen abroad are asked to bear the road construction expenses as a condition for not selling the examination hall, it seems even more unreasonable. Your enthusiasm for roads and benefiting the hometown is deeply admired by overseas compatriots. We hope that you will seek other ways and temporarily retain the examination hall to wait for the opportunity, and announce the full assets and current status of the examination hall so that fellow townsmen groups in Jiangsu can jointly assist in the handling to avoid loss and prevent encroachment. We await your response. With sincere regards."

Jiang Song

Provincial Committee Member Collects Tax Funds in Person

Xie Zhaonan, an accounting specialist sent by the Provincial Department of Finance, has come to Songjiang to personally collect the special national tax funds of Songjiang County. The county magistrate strictly ordered the national tax collection directors Yang and Pan to first arrange for payment. Today, they paid 45,000 yuan in taxes, and more than 100,000 yuan has been paid previously. Compared with the achievements of various counties, Songjiang County is still among the first batch of tax payers. It is heard that the remaining funds must be paid by February 1. Although the harvest in this county is relatively good, the national tax collection is not as good as last year, so the two directors are very anxious.

Suzhou

Economic Oppression Leads to Suicide by Train

Yuan Chunshan, a local man, about 30 years old, had been engaged in business in Shanghai, but failed repeatedly. With the end of the year approaching, he could not maintain his livelihood. On the afternoon of the 28th, at around 3:00 PM, he went to a place near Guanlu Li on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway and lay on the tracks with the intention of committing suicide. When a freight train passed by, he was crushed to death. His feet and head were thrown out of the tracks for a distance of ten zhang, and his brains burst, a tragic sight. Afterwards, the railway police notified the local security, and yesterday (29th) they reported to the local court, which sent personnel to verify that he was indeed crushed to death by the train during his lifetime. A suicide note was found beside him, explaining the circumstances of the suicide. The court ordered the local security to collect the body and wait for relatives to claim it.

Wuxi

Water Tank Explosion Kills Worker

The hot water tank in the stove room of the Qingfeng Yarn Factory in Zhou Shanbang suddenly exploded the other day. At that time, a worker named Li Kunlin was nearby and was scalded. The factory immediately sent him to the Brothers Hospital for treatment, but due to his serious injuries, he died yesterday afternoon at around 3:00 PM. It is heard that the deceased was not married and had only an elderly mother at home who depended on him for a living. His death was tragic.

Lawyer Sues Director Case, Summons Issued

Lawyers Sun Zuhong and Zhu Yunsheng, etc., were fined by the Public Security Bureau for playing donkey games with poker cards at the New World Hotel. Sun et al. refused to accept the verdict and sued Public Security Bureau Director Chen Yuchu and Section Chief Yi Weifan for obstructing freedom. At the same time, they also sued Public Security Bureau Inspector Feng Yimao at the procuratorate for false accusation and defamation. Yesterday (29th) was the court date for the false accusation case. At 2:00 PM, Chief Justice Qian summoned the plaintiffs Sun Zuhong and Zhu Yunsheng, and the defendant Feng Yimao for interrogation. The order was to dismiss them after verification. The Criminal Court also issued four summons signed by Judge Liu Bingzhen, instructing the police to summon the plaintiffs Sun Zuhong and Zhu Yunsheng, and the defendants Chen Yuchu and Yi Weifan, to court at 2:00 PM on February 25th to hear the case of obstructing freedom.

Zhang Honglie Inspects Factories

Zhang Honglie, Director of the Department of Construction of Shandong Province, considering that this county is famous throughout the country as an industrial and commercial area with numerous factories, made a special trip from Shanghai to Wuxi the day before yesterday. On the same day, he visited the Shenxin No. 3 Cotton Mill and other factories. Yesterday (the 29th), accompanied by Qian Hu and other gentlemen, he visited scenic spots such as Meiyuan Garden, Yuantouzhu, and Baojie Bridge. In the afternoon, he went to Changzhou to visit factories to learn from their experiences.

Disaster-Stricken Farmers Conspire to Default on Rent

Since Wuxi County suffered a severe drought last summer, resulting in a poor autumn harvest, the payment of winter rent has been affected. Various granaries and offices have reported meager collection amounts. Furthermore, it has been discovered that tenants from fields marked with "Du Men Li Mei Jing Shang Ye" and other designations have jointly contacted neighboring "Hao Zhu Ju He" and other areas, using the disaster as an excuse to attempt to resist paying rent. The landlords of these granaries and offices, including Yang Baoye, Bao Ziyu Hua, and Cai Yishu, believing that they are secretly colluding and the situation is serious, specially submitted a request to the county government yesterday, requesting a thorough investigation and urging the heads of each area to promptly persuade them to avoid inciting unrest and to ensure the proper payment of rent.

Changzhou

Theft of Rice from a Motorboat Leads to a Fatality

Yang Shilin, a native of Wuxi, owns a motorboat equipped with a 24-horsepower engine. Recently, it was moored near Panjiatang, outside the east gate of Changzhou, to mill rice for the villagers. On the afternoon of the 28th, around 1 PM, a villager found that more than ten catties of rice were missing after milling. Upon searching the boat, the missing rice was found. The villager, believing that someone on the boat had stolen the rice, negotiated with Yang Shilin, the boat owner. Unexpectedly, the worker on the engine became enraged out of embarrassment and grabbed the villager, causing him to fall onto the engine's belt. He was immediately pulled into the machine and crushed to death. The worker, realizing the gravity of the situation, fled the scene. After hearing the news, the local police station dispatched officers to investigate at Dujiang.

Cargo Ship Sinks in Sanjiangying

On the 27th of this month, at 11:00 AM, a cargo ship traveling from a port to Jianbi sank while navigating the waters of Sanjiangying, forced down by adverse winds and currents. It was subsequently spotted by the No. 8 Red Boat from the Jiaoshan Lifesaving Bureau, which rushed to rescue the situation. Two shipowners, Zhou Jiuru and Zhou Yonggui, were fortunately rescued. However, salvaging the sunken ship will not be an easy task.

Tongnan

Riotous Allowance Demands Resolved, Security Team Disarmed

The Second Company of the 19th Security Battalion, stationed in the towns of Xiasha Juyang, Longjia, and Fu'an in Haimen, has been undisciplined and recently rioted over allowance demands. Zheng Yitong, the Administrative Inspector of the Nantong District and concurrently the Security Commander, deemed that the team damaged the military's reputation. On the 27th, he secretly went to Haimen and stationed himself at the Haimen County Government. He secretly ordered Zhang Du, the battalion commander of the Qidong Security Team, and Dong Ruifu, the commander of the Second Industrial Security Battalion, to select capable teams and surround and disarm the riotous company in the Xiasha area. By noon, the situation was fully resolved. The disarmed troops were taken to Fu'an Town and handed over to Chen Guiqing, the battalion commander in charge, to await reorganization. The defense duties for the vacated area are temporarily taken over by the teams that conducted the disarming.

Arson at Dasheng Cotton Mill by Workers

Recently, the Dasheng Cotton Mill in Tangjiaza, Nantong, had a dispute over layoffs due to the adoption of electricity, which has now been resolved. However, workers such as Chen Qiaoying and Qin Jinhou suddenly set fire to the factory. The stationed police discovered the arson and arrested Chen, Qin, and others, handing them over to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation by the county government.

Jiaxing

Adultery and Murder Case in Tanghui Township

Ni Guishou, a farmer from Nanzhangbang, a village in Tanghui Town, Jiaxing, married a woman surnamed Liu from nearby Xishi eight years ago and had a four-year-old son. Liu is currently four to five months pregnant. Recently, Liu had an affair with Ni Guishou's cousin, Daoqing. Guishou repeatedly advised his wife to stop, but she refused. One night, Guishou returned home from outside and saw his wife sleeping with Daoqing. He intended to call others to catch them in the act of adultery, but Daoqing grabbed him, pulled out a sharp knife, and attempted to stab Guishou. Seeing the danger, Guishou cried out for help. Daoqing panicked, dropped the knife, and fled. In a fit of anger, Guishou picked up the knife and stabbed Liu's abdomen three times, causing her intestines to spill out. Realizing the gravity of the situation, Guishou sent his wife to the city hospital for treatment on the 28th. Unfortunately, due to the severity of the injuries, and the fetus in her womb was also sticking a hand out, she could not be saved. Guishou surrendered to the court at 4:00 PM, reporting everything. Liu died late that night.

Special Feature

Enemy or Friend? (4) (Continued)

— Xu Daolin

丨Review of Sino-Japanese Relations丨

(7) Key Points and Paths to Be Recognized and Adopted by China and Japan

Understanding the various errors of China and Japan mentioned above clarifies the reasons for the evolution of the September 18th Incident into a stalemate. It goes without saying that the stalemate should not be prolonged. The opposite of error is truth. By examining the reverse of the points mentioned above, one can discover what China and Japan should recognize and the paths they should take. The above discussion is extremely detailed, so I will only summarize them as follows:

Paths to be Recognized and Adopted by China　The initiative to break the Sino-Japanese stalemate certainly lies with Japan. However, assuming Japan sincerely expresses its intentions, what should China do? I believe that China should recognize that arrogance is not a solution, procrastination is not a solution, stagnation is not a solution, expecting or relying on others is not a solution, and sacrificing reason for emotion is not a solution. The mistakes of the past were due to arrogance, so from now on, the entire country should recognize the facts, have confidence in its own future, and not ignore its own weaknesses. Furthermore, the life of a nation is for thousands of years. Temporary honor and disgrace are common in history as long as they do not affect the fundamentals. Therefore, as long as Japan sincerely seeks a solution, China only needs to demand the abandonment of territorial aggression and the return of the four northeastern provinces. Other modalities need not be rigidly adhered to. Past outstanding issues should be resolved sincerely and mutually beneficially to eliminate obstacles to diplomatic relations. The people should understand the greater good and not make unreasonable demands. The authorities should endure humiliation and bear heavy burdens, demonstrating loyalty. As for expecting international turmoil to benefit China, it must be understood that Japan's victory is not China's blessing, and Japan's defeat or demise is not the blessing of China or East Asia. Currently, since Japan's breakdown of negotiations with London regarding naval reductions, it has been in a tight spot on all sides, becoming the target of public criticism, completely trapped in a state of isolation. Therefore, some people believe that because Japan has committed many unjust acts, it will eventually destroy itself, and China need not suffer temporary pain. China should rather become a rubble field like Belgium, so that Japan may follow Germany's path in the European War and suffer even greater disasters. Therefore, for China's sake, in this situation, it must persist, and should prolong Japan's arrogance to observe its weaknesses. The author believes that the meaning of humanity lies not in mutual obstruction but in coexistence. World progress should value righteousness over emotional impulses. Japan's current recklessness is akin to a madman rushing toward a well. We all see it clearly, but China, based on its inherent concept of righteousness, should only strive for survival through its own efforts, without taking advantage of others' benefits. It should be known that Japan's actions, even if they harm others, ultimately harm itself, while China should be upright, uphold justice, and save others as well as itself. If the situation allows, it should also open a path to enlightenment for Japan, without harboring malicious intentions. If Japan does not force China to perish together, China should seek survival through a path to life and not follow the wild currents to collapse together, mutually dragging each other into error. If it is said that retaining a strong enemy can motivate the people's ambition, in my opinion, as long as the people resolutely revitalize themselves with the determination to be reborn today after dying yesterday, and no longer become as undisciplined and weak as before, disrupting their own progress, they can revive even without external threats. As for still observing the international situation or harboring reliance on others after suffering lessons, it is not only unwise but also demonstrates China's lack of ambition and awareness. For example, even now, some people pay attention to Japan's attitude toward the Nine-Power Treaty and the Washington Treaty and react with joy or sorrow accordingly. However, it must be understood that if the preservation of territorial integrity and the open-door policy depend on international agreements, this is already China's great danger. The reason why the powers made these agreements is not to plan for China. On the surface, it is nothing more than maintaining equilibrium and protecting commerce, but in reality, it is the only method for imperialism to deal with semi-colonies. If China cannot revive through its own efforts and still relies on these treaties, then as the situation changes, it may be a prelude to partition or joint administration. It must be understood that Japan's current recklessness is to turn China into a protectorate, demanding hegemony, while the Western powers, regarding a China that cannot strengthen itself, envision the outcome as partition or joint administration, with the slogan of equal opportunity. From China's standpoint, whether it is exclusive or joint occupation, it is an unacceptable harm to the nation. The only way for China to plan for itself is to rely on its own strength, endure hardship, and strive for survival. It should decisively resolve current obstacles, especially the conflicts with Japan, and quickly seek to eliminate them, while not relaxing in the slightest on the essential plan for self-strengthening and self-preservation. It must be known that only when one stands up on one's own feet is there security. As for being driven by grief and anger, swayed by emotions, and echoing the slogans of the late Qing Dynasty, thinking that it is better to perish at the hands of Europe and America than at the hands of Japan, it must be understood that China is an independent country, and not an inch of its land can be destroyed by any foreign nationality. Therefore, everything else seems secondary, and the only requirement is to maintain national independence and integrity.

Paths to be Recognized and Adopted by Japan　What Japan should first recognize is that only with an independent China can there be an East Asia for East Asians. Therefore, the first imperative is to thoroughly support China's genuine independence, which is Japan's enduring national policy. With an independent China standing shoulder to shoulder with advanced Japan in an equal position, Japan can then make good use of its "special position and interests in East Asia" (Hirota's words), and China can also fulfill its mission to East Asia. Secondly, it should be known that times have changed, and the policies of the past are no longer applicable. To thoroughly renew Sino-Japanese relations, it should abandon military force and focus on cultural cooperation, abandon territorial aggression and replace it with mutually beneficial economic cooperation, abandon attempts at political control, and combine with China through moral and emotional bonds. Thirdly, it should be known that in the past tension in Sino-Japanese relations, if China had 40% of the responsibility, Japan should have at least 60%. Since the September 18th Incident, Japan has intensified tension with international communities in order to achieve its purposes. This is due to Japan's excessive optimism about distant and unrealized ambitions, and excessive pessimism about near and feasible solutions. We believe that if the Sino-Japanese problem were quickly resolved, it could at least clear a large part of the turbulence, and the resolution of the Sino-Japanese problem only requires a swift shift in Japan's mind. If Japan can truly realize that persisting in this deadlock is not a plan for shared danger, and stop covering it up with empty words, stop fabricating various false reasons, and stop acting self-satisfied and self-justifying, it should earnestly express the sincerity of "preserving China's unity" and "absolutely not hindering China's independence or interests and not intending to harm them" (words from the Japanese Foreign Ministry's statement and Hirota's talks), decisively return the four northeastern provinces, making them belong to China's territory. At the same time, it should resolve outstanding issues between China and Japan. This negotiation should, of course, be initiated by Japan, but direct negotiations between the two countries are also acceptable. After an agreement is reached, China will report to the League of Nations. The League of Nations, in order to maintain peace, will be happy to accept. At the same time, the reason for Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations will have been eliminated, so it should rejoin the League of Nations to eliminate the various difficult problems caused by its withdrawal from the League. In this way, the ill feelings between China and Japan can certainly disappear, and the dark clouds of war threatening the world will immediately clear. All of humanity will benefit from Japan's actions. This will not damage Japan's dignity or original stance, and on the other hand, it can avoid endless future thorns. For Japan's sake, this is the only proper national policy.

VIII. Conclusion: The One Who Tied the Bell Must Untie It

This article is neither a strategist's eloquent argument nor a specialist's meticulous treatise. The author is confident that it does not contain the slightest prejudice or preconception, and there are no taboos. It simply discusses the true interests of both countries, as well as the East Asian situation and world peace. What is pointed out is not some profound theory, but a kind of ordinary platitude. However, the truth of the world often lies in these ordinary principles. If the politicians of both countries have broad minds and deep insight, they should disregard everything, eliminate obstacles, and rise up to implement the path mentioned in the previous paragraph to break the current stalemate. However, this responsibility lies almost entirely with Japan, because regardless of the first half of the problem, the obstruction of all solutions is the result of Japan's refusal to accept any advice. Since then, third countries or other organizations can only stand aside, and China, being in a state of humiliation of occupied territory, has no possibility of breaking the stalemate. I believe that the Japanese should know that the thorns ahead were all created by Japan itself. If they turn back now, the flat road will appear immediately. An ancient Chinese saying goes: "The one who tied the bell must untie it," so the responsibility for breaking the deadlock must ultimately be borne by Japan.

In short, whether in terms of history, geography, or national relations, the relationship between China and Japan should be more than that of lips and teeth, really being nations that live and die together, coexist and perish together. Will they ultimately be enemies and perish together? Or will they restore friendship and jointly shoulder the mission of the times? This depends on whether the people and authorities of both countries, especially Japan, have the courage to recognize the facts, pull back from the precipice, and the wisdom to clear away obstacles and plan for the long term. (The End)

This Year's Children's Year Expanded Publicity Campaign for Children's Day

Central and Local Governments Hold Preparations Separately

Last year, the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association suggested to the National Child Welfare Association to request the central government to designate this year as "China Children's Year" in order to promote national children's welfare and strengthen the race. This measure is of great significance. The National Child Welfare Association and the Municipal Children's Welfare Association are organizing the "China Children's Year Preparatory Committee" in order to promote an expanded publicity campaign as the Children's Day of April 4th is fast approaching. Here is an overview of the process and implementation methods:

The Course of Preparations　Civilized countries in the modern world often hold Children's Years to promote children's welfare. The purpose of the Children's Year is to arouse national public attention to children's undertakings, so that everyone has the concept of loving children and bears the responsibility of loving children. At the same time, it also makes children across the country understand their own position, strive to improve, and strive to move forward. Its significance is extremely important. On November 15, 1933, the National Child Welfare Association approved the proposal of the Children's Welfare Association and submitted a request to the National Government to promote the year 1934 as Children's Year. On February 12, 1934, it was instructed by the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to inform the National Government that the period of the Children's Year should be changed to 1935 due to preparatory reasons. On May 14th of last year, the association drafted an organizational outline for the Central and Local Preparatory Committees for the China Children's Year and requested the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to submit it to the Ministry of Education for review. The Ministry of Education agreed to adopt it as a reference.

Central Children's Year　The organizational outline for the Children's Year drafted by the association is divided into central and local categories. The work of the Central Children's Year Preparatory Committee includes: (1) publishing a China Children's Year Handbook, (2) formulating China Children's Year slogans, (3) formulating China Children's Year songs, (3) formulating China Children's Year declaration (published on New Year's Day), (5) requesting the National Government to issue a circular to all major newspapers across the country to publish a special issue on the opening of China Children's Year, (6) holding an opening ceremony for China Children's Year in the capital, (7) holding a Children's Year oath ceremony in the capital (all of the above are on New Year's Day), (8) broadcasting lectures on children's welfare issues on the radio every Sunday, (9) requesting the National Government to issue a circular to all major newspapers across the country to publish more special children's issues, (10) planning a fund for the China Child Welfare Association to build a clubhouse, (11) collecting and reviewing children's toys from all over the country, (12) collecting and reviewing children's reading materials from all over the country, (13) formulating a China Children's Day song for the Ministry of Education to reference, (14) preparing for a national children's representative audience with the Chairman of the National Government, (15) holding a national children's beauty contest, (16) holding a national children's sports meeting, (17) holding a national children's competition, (18) holding a national children's speech contest, (19) holding a national children's concert, (10) holding a national children's military equipment exhibition (21) initiating a national children's tour, (22) compiling a China Children's Year report, (23) others.

Local Children's Year　The work of the Local Children's Year Preparatory Committee includes: (1) holding an opening ceremony for Children's Year (January 1st), (2) holding a children's patriotic oath ceremony (January 1st), (3) holding a children's welfare lecture every week, (4) holding a parents' meeting, mothers' meeting, or parents' education research meeting every week, (5) holding a children's toy exhibition, (6) holding a children's reading materials exhibition, (7) raising donations for local child welfare organizations, (8) holding a Children's Day celebration (April 4th), (9) holding a children's beauty contest, (10) holding a children's sports meeting, (11) holding a children's competition, (12) holding a children's speech contest, (13) holding a children's concert, (14) holding a children's variety show, (15) holding a military equipment exhibition, (16) initiating a children's parade, (17) encouraging children to participate in local construction work (such as repairing roads, bridges, water conservancy, irrigation, etc.), (18) encouraging children to visit patients and wounded soldiers, (19) encouraging children to donate to poor children, (20) encouraging children to organize associations for loving and using domestic goods, (21) others.
