50,000 for Emergency Drought Relief in Various Provinces, 50,000 for Emergency Banditry Relief in Jiangxi

According to Central News Agency, since its establishment, the Urgent Relief and Donation Association has worked very hard to handle various universal donations, and has received a total of more than 100,000 donations, which has been reported in various newspapers. Ministry of Communications Develops Telephone Plan

Long-Distance Telephone Service in Nine Provinces

According to Xin Xin News Agency, the Ministry of Communications plans to install long-distance telephone service in nine provinces to facilitate domestic communication. Chen Gengfa, the Chief Engineer of the Shanghai-Hankou Line, has been dispatched to Hankou to survey the route from Hankou to Qiupu, and Li Guohua, the Chief Engineer of the Qinghu Line, has been dispatched to survey the route from Qiupu to Nanjing. It is learned that the two gentlemen, Chen and Li, have completed the route survey and are now proceeding to the second step of surveying. As soon as the survey is completed, they will begin erecting poles and stringing wires. It is estimated that the construction of the project can begin at the beginning of next month. The Jinghan Line is expected to be completed and open to communication in six months. The full completion of communication in all nine provinces will not be possible until two years later at the earliest. However, the Ministry of Communications believes that the construction of long-distance telephones in various provinces and the establishment of wireless telephones require a large amount of money, which is difficult to raise in a short period of time. It has submitted a request to the Executive Yuan to allocate 800,000 yuan for application. It is learned that the funding has been approved by the Executive Yuan meeting to be drawn from the second item of national reserve funds, and it has been approved for implementation by the Central Political Conference. Therefore, the construction plan for long-distance telephone service in nine provinces can proceed step by step.

National Wireless Telephone Service

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, in order to develop the domestic wireless radio business, the Ministry of Communications purchased wireless radio parts and materials in the United Kingdom last year with the Boxer Indemnity funds allocated by the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Association. It designated Shanghai, Nanjing, Hankou, Tianjin, and Beiping as the first five places to install telephone service. Since the parts and materials were purchased and returned to China, the Ministry ordered the Zhenru International Wireless Radio Station to set up a general station. At the end of last year, it conducted several test calls with the aforementioned locations, and the sound was clear and there was no obstruction of radio waves. The station's situation in Shanghai is reported and broadcast daily. According to news from the station, the Ministry of Communications is currently planning to expand the installation in major cities across the country. After March, it plans to develop overseas and establish wireless radio station communication internationally.

Consul in Houston Reports Tung Oil to Be Phased Out

Countries Compete to Plant Tung Trees

Tung oil is a unique product of China and an important raw material for the paint industry. In recent years, it has occupied an important position in export trade. In order to achieve self-sufficiency in raw materials, various countries are planting tung trees, with the United States being particularly diligent. When the time is right, China's tung oil industry will inevitably be naturally eliminated. The International Trade Bureau recently received a report from the Consul in Houston regarding overseas tung tree planting, excerpts of which are as follows: Tung oil was first imported into the United States as far back as 1869. At that time, the American Consul General in Hankou explained the value and uses of tung oil, and the United States government began to pay special attention. As a result, the Department of Agriculture, the Paint Industry Association, various university agricultural colleges, the Tung Oil Association, and others actively conducted research. Since 1902, tung seeds have been continuously shipped to various provinces in the United States for widespread planting. Publications on tung tree planting are frequently published. According to statistics from the U.S. Department of Commerce, the area planted with tung trees in various provinces has reached more than 44,000 acres. The Ford Motor Company, considering tung oil essential for automobiles and airplanes, has opened a 200-acre tung tree planting farm to collect seeds and press oil themselves, eliminating the need to purchase from China. England, France, Germany, and other countries have also made efforts, but with little effect. After the United States successfully tested planting, various countries followed suit. China has been actively purchasing tung seeds from the United States and the UK, with the United Kingdom being particularly enthusiastic. In 1927, the Oil Affairs Advisory Committee of the British Royal Society cooperated with paint industrialists to purchase tung seeds from the United States for planting in various colonies. According to recent reports, Australia, New Zealand, India, Burma, Ceylon, Malaya, the Union of South Africa, Sudan, the West Indies, Honduras, and other British territories have all achieved good results, and the future is immeasurable. In addition, Argentina has planted 50,000 tung trees, Paraguay 30,000, and Russia has planted 900 acres. Currently, there are plans to plant 36,000 acres in 1937. Other countries, such as Italy, Central and South American countries, the Dutch East Indies, and the Belgian Congo and Morocco in East Africa, have purchased large quantities of tung seeds from the United States for trial planting.

Merchant Mariners General Assembly Submits a Request to the Ministry to Implement Seafarer Insurance

The issue of seafarer insurance was previously raised by Shanghai shipping merchants, who advocated that all sailors, stokers, and others on ships be insured for life and accident, so that in the event of a maritime accident, the compensation could be used as part of the support. However, this matter has not yet been realized. The Merchant Marine Drivers Association has submitted a request to the Ministry of Commerce, requesting implementation. The original submission is as follows:

Submission regarding the dangers of seafarer life, requesting that all shipping companies be ordered to uniformly insure seafarers' lives and accidents to prevent unforeseen circumstances and provide for subsequent arrangements. It is noted that seafaring is inherently dangerous and cannot be compared to the safety of other occupations. Those who engage in this profession struggle daily against relentless storms and waves, and collisions and accidents are ever-present dangers. Maritime disasters and losses are thus specific terms. In recent years, maritime accidents have been frequent, and shipwrecks are often heard of. For example, the recent sinking of the Taishan Tongfu ship resulted in no survivors among the crew, causing grief to all who heard of it. However, the dead are gone, and what about the living? If good methods are not devised to provide security, then seafarers will view seafaring with trepidation. Although the Maritime Commerce Law has provisions for seafarers who die in the line of duty, shipowners often go bankrupt due to the sinking of the ship, making them unable to provide support, or they are uncharitable in their hearts and make various excuses, causing the bereaved families to run around appealing, which is truly pitiful. The disputes over the Tongfu ship today are a clear example. It is noted that among the Chinese insurance companies currently in China, there are those who underwrite seafarer life and accident insurance. The premium per ship per year is only a few hundred yuan. In the event of an accident, compensation can be received for support. For shipowners, the burden is very light, avoiding liability, and for families, funds can be obtained immediately for subsequent arrangements. This is truly a good policy that benefits both parties. It is therefore urgently submitted, requesting that all shipping companies be ordered to uniformly insure seafarers' lives and accidents to prevent unforeseen circumstances and provide for subsequent arrangements, which would truly be a benefit. Respectfully submitted, etc.

Sharp Fall in Japanese Currency

One Hundred Chinese Dollars Can Be Exchanged for One Hundred Twenty-Nine Yuan and Fifty Fen

Yesterday's Japanese-language Mainichi Shimbun reported that the Japanese gold market had been gradually changing its tone for several days. On the 28th, it suddenly plummeted. This is due to the year-end settlement of accounts for the Lunar New Year, which requires a large amount of cash, and the settlement of the Sino-Soviet Railway negotiations, the payment of compensation, and the repayment of the British goods debentures of the South Manchuria Railway, which have contributed to this. Based on the current situation, it is speculated that the Japanese currency may fall to 150 yuan, which is not impossible.

Hou Shinian's Collection of Seals of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Will is Published

Finely Printed and Distributed by the Commercial Press

Central News Agency reports that the Collection of Seals of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Will is composed of twenty-five sentences from Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will, each sentence forming a seal. Each seal is made in a different style according to the meaning of the sentence, and the carving methods are carefully avoided from being the same. In addition to conforming to the Qin and Han dynasties, it also takes inspiration from bells, tripods, coins, and roof tiles. There are also inscriptions by more than twenty gentlemen, including Wu Zhihui, Yu Youren, Cai Yuanpei, Tan Zekai, Xu Beihong, and Wang Yiting. It is not only praised as a masterpiece of modern seal carving and can serve as a model for beginners, but it is also the first work of art from the Party and the country's literature, most suitable for decorating living rooms. It has been made into metal plates by the Shanghai Commercial Press, mounted into artistic four-foot scrolls, and officially distributed by branches in various places. It is reported that Comrade Hou Shinian, the author, is currently working in the Central Party Headquarters.

Ministry of Finance Explains Stamp Tax Method for Triplicate Invoices

Only Stamp the Copy Given to the Customer

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Candy, Biscuit, and Canned Goods Association asking for clarification on whether the second and third copies of triplicate invoices and the covers of invoice books should be stamped. The Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance on the matter, which replied this month: "Your telegram is noted. It is confirmed that for triplicate invoices in the form of bound books used by stores, as long as the copy given to the customer is stamped with sufficient stamps as required, the remaining two copies and the cover need not be stamped again. This was previously reviewed and approved in September of the 19th year of the Republic of China based on an inquiry from the China Bookstore and has been circulated as a record. Please be informed." This approval.

The Municipal Party Headquarters Orders All Public Organizations to Create Monthly Expenditure and Revenue Registers

To Ensure Accuracy and Maintain Public Trust

The Dagong News reports that the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters Executive Committee yesterday issued an order to all public organizations, stating: "To ensure compliance, it is found that public organizations in this city often do not keep accurate records of income and expenditure, and they are not sincerely open to the public. Leaders may even abuse their authority at will. Once reported, they often make excuses and evade responsibility, resulting in numerous disputes. In order to rectify public movements, the Association has specially stipulated that all public organizations must keep detailed records of all income and expenditure, preserve all receipts separately, and create and publish monthly registers to ensure accuracy and maintain public trust. At the end of each month, the Association will send personnel to various organizations to review the accounts at any time. If fraud is discovered as a result of the audit, or if the organization fails to comply with the order, the responsible person will be severely punished in order to deter those who engage in wrongful activities and benefit public movements. In addition to circulating this order, the Association hereby orders you to comply and not deviate in the slightest. This is of utmost importance.

This order is issued by Standing Committee Members Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, and Tong Xingbai.

Part of the Workers at the Seeking New Machine Shipbuilding Plant Strike Yesterday

Because the Request to Reinstate Three Dismissed Workers Was Ineffective

The Xin Xin News reports that more than 300 workers are employed at the Seeking New Machine Shipbuilding Plant on Jichang Street in Nanshi. On the 26th of this month, the plant manager (McTileo) dismissed three apprentices, No. 849, No. 844, etc., which caused opposition from more than 80 workers. At 8 a.m. yesterday, the workers requested the manager to reinstate the dismissed workers, but to no avail. They first went on strike, then formally announced a strike. The Shipbuilding Industry Association of the First District of this city was notified and immediately sent Director Wu Qiulin to negotiate with the plant manager and the second-in-command, but was also rejected. The workers then gathered at the Shipbuilding Industry Association of the First District yesterday to discuss solutions. A resolution was passed to propose three conditions: (1) immediately reinstate the dismissed workers, (2) pay wages as usual during the strike, and (3) do not dismiss workers without reason in the future. At the same time, the circumstances of the strike were submitted to the municipal party and government agencies and the General Labor Union, requesting assistance. It is also heard that after receiving the news, the Municipal Public Security Bureau specially sent four policemen to the plant yesterday to protect it, in order to avoid incidents.

Improvements in Training of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps

Colonel Grier, Commander of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps of the Shanghai International Settlement, has submitted his report for the past year to the Municipal Council. In it, he considers the prior announcement of inspections of various units to be inappropriate. He proposes inviting the British military commander to inspect the team at any time so that the training can be effectively recognized. Also, past overall inspections have been too formal and of little military value, and should be changed to a column-style march.

Increased Use of Officers In the past, the Corps was only an organization of one battalion, which was extremely inconvenient for training. Now, one quartermaster officer and one battalion officer have been added. In addition, one advisor should be appointed for the Russian battalion (already approved) and two adjutants (one already approved). According to the new organization, there is one cavalry regiment, one artillery team, one special team, and three infantry battalions. The first and second battalions are volunteer members, and the third battalion is Russian members.

Rectification of Firearms Commander Grier advocates that a European and American ordnance specialist should be hired to be responsible for repairing ordnance and supervising workers. The appointment of this person is currently under consideration by the board of directors. Additional Barracks The new house built on top of the garage will be completed soon. In peacetime, it can be used as a dedicated training room for each team and group. In times of mobilization, it can provide accommodation for 350 members. The quartermaster's storage room and courier room have also been completed. The Corps Club has also been rebuilt.

Training Needs The commander pays close attention to whether the training is effective. The roads in the settlement are too narrow, so in practice, it is mostly theoretical explanations. Defensive and flatland warfare must undergo the same training without distinction. Therefore, there must be long-term personnel in charge of this matter. Last year, personnel from the British Army and the US Navy were borrowed to serve as firearm combat instructors for 15 nights. 150 officers were trained, and most were able to pass on what they had learned to the members they commanded. The results were quite satisfactory. Infantry is the backbone of the military, but its training is more monotonous and difficult. Therefore, it is urgent to add one formal military battalion commander to each of the first and second battalions so that the training can be effective.

Target Practice Last year's target practice results were generally satisfactory. However, during target practice, there was a lack of experienced instructors to point out mistakes at any time. Therefore, there were often repeated misses, which led to discouragement. After the establishment of a manager in the target range, a lot of waste was saved. The targets are now made of waste materials by carpenters. The light artillery team, with the kindness of the British military commander, went to Hong Kong on a British warship last year to practice live-fire shooting. However, the team's cannons are too old, and ammunition cannot be purchased. Replacements are needed within two years. It is best to replace them with the British-style three-inch white cannons, which are not expensive, easy to train with, and most suitable for application.

Recruitment Difficulties Currently, there is a shortage of about 100 British and American members in the first and second battalions. Commander Grier's intention is that it is best to train a smaller number of members who can be mobilized in times of small emergencies and at the same time prepare several groups of trained reserves who will not be called up until commerce is completely at a standstill. In this way, both corps affairs and commerce can be taken care of.

Announcement by the Survey Bureau Regarding the Dredging of the Gaohangsha New Waterway

Navigation Announcement No. 13 of the Hydrographic Survey Bureau of the Ministry of the Navy states: The two temporary lightships in the Gaohangsha New Waterway in the Yangtze River Estuary, China's East Coast, have been withdrawn. Refer to Navigation Announcements Nos. 162 and 170 (temporary announcements) of the 23rd year. Location: In the Gaohangsha New Waterway, approximately 121 degrees 31 minutes East longitude and 31 degrees 21 minutes North latitude. Explanation: The two temporary lightships, which were specially installed for the dredging project, will be withdrawn on January 26th of this year. Note: The dredging project is still in progress. All vessels should pass the dredger from the south, reduce speed, and sound one long blast of the whistle when approaching the dredger. Relevant charts: Hydrographic Chart No. 507 of the Ministry of the Navy. Announcing Agency: Shanghai Harbor Master. Note: The directions listed in this Navigation Announcement are calculated from true north (0 degrees), turning clockwise to 359 degrees. However, the directions of the lights are calculated from the sea. The range of light intensity is based on clear weather. The fog signal is only used in foggy weather. Depth records will be explained separately if necessary and are calculated based on the benchmark plane used for large-scale charts. (January 24, 24th year)

Health and Social Bureaus Ban Tooth Protection Association

Ordered the Association to Cease Operations Immediately, Joint Letter to the Municipal Party Department for Reference

According to the Guomin News Agency, a Tooth Protection Association was discovered in the city last year. Its organizational content was not very legal, and the health authorities ordered it to correct this. As the association still has some non-compliant aspects, the Health Bureau, together with the Social Bureau, has banned it and sent a letter to the Municipal Party Department for reference. The original letter is extracted below: "After investigation, the China Age Tooth Protection Association has neither applied for permission to establish itself in accordance with the regulations on supervising social organizations in this city, nor has it complied with the instructions of this Health Bureau: (1) The medical part of the association should be permanently responsible for dentures by a formal dentist, and Ying Yongfeng should not impersonate a dentist or doctor. (2) Dentists who have not been approved and registered by this city shall not be employed. (3) All promotional advertisements of the association shall not contain false or exaggerated information, etc. According to recent investigations, the former employed dentist Lin Qingping has long since resigned, and the medical part is, in fact, still unauthorizedly diagnosed by denture maker Ying Yongfeng. In addition to arbitrarily publishing false and exaggerated advertisements in various newspapers, the association also produces special publications in the News Evening Post, doing its best to make false deceptions. All of these are in stark contrast to the three restrictions previously opened by this Health Bureau. Furthermore, the membership fees stipulated in the association's charter are as high as hundreds of dollars per person. Since the association has not obtained legal person status in accordance with the law and official instructions, nor is it an approved formal commercial savings institution or commercial insurance institution, the huge amount of public funds collected has not been found to have detailed safekeeping measures, and the interests of members are virtually unprotected. It seems that this is close to cheating and defrauding money, and it should be strictly banned. In addition to ordering the association to immediately stop activities and separately report the completion for approval, it must not be delayed and held accountable. The corresponding letter is hereby sent for reference to the Executive Committee of the Kuomintang Shanghai Special Municipality."

Ningbo Boat Filled with Smuggled Salt Under Huangsha

Water Patrol Team Discovers the Situation, Detains Yu Caiwu and Wei Guoying

At about 2:00 PM yesterday, Li Wenhan, a patrol officer of the 4th Squad of the Water Patrol Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, led several police officers on a patrol of the Jiangwan Yunzaobang Pudong area. They spotted a Ningbo boat, Municipal Photo No. 8602, fully loaded with burlap bags, speeding towards them. However, when the crew of the boat saw the patrol boat approaching, their expressions suddenly became flustered and suspicious. They immediately jumped onto the boat. Under search, it was found that the burlap bags carried on the boat had sand on the top few bags, but the bottom ones were all smuggled salt, the value of which was very large. Therefore, the crew of the boat, Yu Caiwu, and Wei Guoying from Pudong, were detained and taken back to the team along with the evidence. Under strict interrogation, Yu Caiwu confessed that he was 35 years old and from Pudong. The burlap bags were shipped from Dinghai, Ningbo, and were intended to be unloaded in Yangshupu. The ship owner, Yu Afa, contracted for the shipment. They only knew that it contained yellow sand and did not know that a large amount of smuggled salt was secretly hidden inside. He asked for leniency, etc. Wei Guoying confessed that he was 64 years old and had been working in the Xiangyuanfeng Rice Shop in Songjiang. This time, he escorted 400 dan of rice to the Baotongchang Rice Shop in Dinghai, Ningbo. Later, because the boat came to Shanghai, he took the opportunity to hitch a ride but did not know that there were illegal activities on the boat, etc. The team was ordered to prepare a document and send it to the headquarters for review.

Shanghai's Real Estate Industry Extremely Depressed Under the Cloud of Economic Recession

Prices Plummet, Transactions Stagnate

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, Shanghai is the only major commercial port in China and a well-known commercial port in the world. The market is prosperous, and the population is large. The total value of real estate in the city was estimated to be approximately 200 million yuan in national currency last year. Now, affected by the market recession, the real estate industry is extremely depressed, prices have plummeted, and transactions have completely stagnated. The Xin Sheng News Agency reporter learned from real estate merchants that the main reason for the decline of the real estate industry is the bankruptcy of the rural economy and the impact on shops, resulting in a sharp drop in land prices. All real estate merchants are unwilling to sell, resulting in stagnant transactions. For example, recently, a certain piece of land with a total of two mu on the eastern end of Nanking Road, Huilo Company, which belongs to foreigners, wanted to sell it, asking for 1.5 million taels. However, the foreigners who intended to buy it initially offered 950,000 yuan and finally 1 million yuan, resulting in no deal. However, the asking price of 1.5 million taels is not too high. Based on this, the decline of Shanghai real estate can be imagined. The eastern part of the Public Concession is a factory area, the western part is a residential area, and the central part is a business area. Real estate transactions used to be quite frequent, so it has a great relationship with the entire finance and can affect various industries. Now that real estate transactions have stagnated, the impact is not small, but it is expected that it will not be difficult to recover in the future.

Public Works Department Raises Roads to Prevent Huangpu River High Tide

Dredging Bureau Announced Tide Times Yesterday, Warehouses Along the River Prepared

The Dredging Bureau announced last week that the Huangpu River would have a high tide on the 4th and 5th of next month, and low-lying areas might be flooded. Now, the Engineering Department of the Public Concession Bureau has raised the roads at the request of merchants along the river (from the Jiujiang Road intersection to the Guangdong Road intersection) to prevent flooding. Warehouses on both sides of the river are also preparing in advance. Yesterday, a reporter from the Industry and Commerce News Agency learned about the situation and recorded it below.

Public Works Department Raises Roads

The area along the river from the Jiujiang Road intersection to the Guangdong Road intersection (east of Sichuan Road) has always been very low-lying. Whenever a high tide occurs, households along the road are at risk of being flooded, and the impact on the bank vaults is even greater. The Engineering Department of the Public Concession Bureau has raised the roads by eight inches to three feet to prevent flooding. Those that have already been raised include the Four Banks Preparatory Vault, the Telephone Bureau, Mitsui & Co., J. L. Morrison & Co., the Jianghai Customs, the Continental Bank, the East Asia Bank, the Bank of China (new location), the China & South Sea Bank, HSBC, and more than ten other locations. Those that have not yet been completed include the Exchange Bureau, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the Bank of Communications, the Central Bank, Citibank, Mitsui Bank, Chase Bank, and Mobil Oil, about ten locations. According to reporters from the Engineering Department, the roads that have been raised must be completed within three or four days.

Tide Times and Heights

The reporter interviewed Mr. Chadley, Chief Engineer of the Dredging Bureau yesterday. According to him, the high tide will definitely occur as scheduled. (1) February 4 (i.e., the Lunar New Year's Day): The tide will rise from 11:49 AM and become stronger from 12:44 PM. The current speed will reach 2.0 nautical miles per hour. By 1:19 PM, it will have reached its highest point, reaching 10 feet and 6.4 inches. (2) February 5 (i.e., the Beginning of Spring Festival): The high tide will occur from 11:39 AM and become stronger from 1:21 PM. The current speed will reach 2.2 nautical miles per hour. By 1:57 PM, it will have reached its highest point, reaching 10 feet and 1.8 inches. During the high tides on these two days, if there is wind surge, the tide may backflow from the sewers and flood the roads in particularly low-lying areas of the port.

Warehouses Along the River Prepare

The warehouses on both sides of the Huangpu River have specially raised the bottom feet of the stored goods in advance to prevent water immersion due to the high tides on those two days. The warehouses have also sent letters to the customers to pick up the goods that should be picked up as soon as possible, otherwise, they will not be responsible for the damage caused by water immersion. According to reporters, the warehouses that have been raised include Dada, Ningshao, Qichang, etc., and the warehouses along the river in Hongkou.

Continuous Heavy Frost, Still Warm Weather in the City

Agricultural Pests Will Prolong Their Lives

There has been continuous heavy frost and still warm weather in the port recently. According to observations by astronomers, this phenomenon is rare in recent years. This climate is partly caused by the severe cold in the Americas and other places. Around spring, all parts of China will also turn to severe cold, and there is a risk of so-called "spring cold." Geographers speculate that the lack of three inches of snow during this cold season will cause a lot of hindrance to crops because the weather is too warm and pests can prolong their lives. During this period, farmers should loosen the soil to compensate for the lack of good weather.

China Kunlun Tobacco Company Announced Liquidation Yesterday Morning

The Reason is that the Market is in Recession and There are Daily Losses

According to Huadong News Agency, China Kunlun Tobacco Co., Ltd. at No. 43, Ou Jia Road, (not Kunlun Tobacco Company on Huacheng Road) was founded in the 20th year of the Republic of China and was established with joint investment from shareholders. The capital was 20 yuan per share, a total of 1,500 shares, and the actual amount received was 30,000 yuan. The manager was Yu Kunshan. It produced various cigarettes such as Hao Shi, Da Halo, Xiao Halo, and Bee Butterfly. The sales in the market were still good, and it was thriving for a while. Recently, due to the impact of the market recession, the released accounts were difficult to collect, the capital was limited, and the turnover was inflexible. They had to stop business yesterday morning and hire Zhao Zuwei, Lu Dingming, lawyers and accountants to announce liquidation. Afterwards, according to reporters from Huadong News Agency, the company's losses were not much, and it is expected to return 60-70% to creditors. As for the completion of the liquidation, it will have to wait until the Lunar New Year next spring. The announcement issued by Zhao Zuwei Lawyer and Lu Dingming Accountant is recorded as follows: According to the board of directors of China Kunlun Tobacco Co., Ltd., the company is suffering from daily losses due to the impact of the market recession, which is difficult to maintain. It has no choice but to entrust representatives to announce the liquidation of the current accounts. In addition to being entrusted by this lawyer, etc., a joint representative notice is hereby issued: Anyone who owes the company or the company owes money is requested to come to register and pay separately within fourteen days of the newspaper publication. Overdue will not be dealt with. Creditors will be regarded as giving up on their own, and debtors will have to be prosecuted. This is hereby announced.

Yesterday Afternoon, Haiyan Ship Collided with Civilian Boat in Front of the New Customs

Boatman Fell into the Water and Rescued by Sampan, Sailboat Destroyed and Stranded in Pudong, Hwa-An Import Almost Collided

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Wenzhou liner Haiyan caused an accident in the Huangpu River yesterday, damaging a civilian boat. When the ship turned around, it almost collided with the Hwa-An, resulting in a disaster. The situation is described in detail below.

Advance to Wenzhou

The Haiyan was originally scheduled to depart from Shanghai to Wenzhou today. However, because the ship was scheduled to depart on the Lunar New Year's Day, the company temporarily advanced the departure by one day, so it departed for Wenzhou at noon yesterday. Passengers taking this ship to Wenzhou were full, and more than 80 male and female actors, including Xiao Sanmazi, who were going to Wenzhou to perform, also set off on the Haiyan. At 11:45 yesterday, it weighed anchor and set sail from the Jinliyuan Wharf. Unexpectedly, it collided with a civilian boat in front of the New Customs Wharf.

Collision with Civilian Boat

When the Haiyan was sailing in the river in front of the Customs, a civilian boat was sailing from north to south. When it approached, the Haiyan pulled its whistle to order the boat to give way. However, due to the high wind and rapid tide, the civilian boat wanted to turn around but could not. Seeing this situation, the captain of the Haiyan wanted to turn aside, but there were other ships on the river. If he did not give way, the civilian boat would be broken into two pieces. He had no choice but to stop and retreat slightly, and the stern of the civilian boat slightly collided with the bow of the Haiyan, which was damaged. The boat was flooded, and the boat was about to sink. The boatman at the stern fell into the Huangpu River, and the goods in the boat were also scattered in the river.

Stop to Help Rescue

At the time of the accident, it was exactly 12:10. The Haiyan immediately stopped and anchored in the river to rescue the boatman who had fallen into the water. Immediately, a sampan threw a lifebuoy and dragged the boatman, but it could not be pulled into the sampan for a while. Later, another sailboat pulled up the boatman who had fallen into the water and rescued him into the boat. The damaged civilian boat was towed by a small fire boat of the water patrol police station to the shore of Pudong and grounded on the beach to avoid sinking. The rescued boatman was sent to the water patrol police station. The loss of the floating goods in the river is not yet known. The civilian boat has reported to the water patrol police station.

Turn Around and Export

At 12:30, the Haiyan weighed anchor and turned around, intending to turn to Lujiazui and export from the Wusongkou. However, the hull was close to the shore of Pudong, and the bottom was blocked by the shallow shore and could not move. The Haiyan reversed and retreated, lying across the river in front of the New Customs. At this time, Zhi Da and Da Yu passed by one after another. The third ship was the Hwa-An of the Chang-An Company, which imported. When it arrived in front of the New Customs, it was blocked by the Haiyan. The two ships were close to each other, and those who saw it were in danger. The Haiyan urgently raised the ball to block the Hwa-An from advancing slowly, and the captain of the Hwa-An immediately stopped and urgently threw double anchors to stop the hull, and the distance was barely a hair's breadth. The Hwa-An hung the yellow flag to import because there were sick passengers in the ship. The doctor ship of the harbor inspection office went to test it when it anchored.

Vice President of the Central Bank, Chen Xing, in Debt Dispute

Yan Zhumeizeng filed a lawsuit and Chen replied that he only owed a thousand gold or so.

Chen Xing, Vice President of the Central Bank, recently also concurrently assumed the position of Director of the Shanghai Mint after the resignation of Lu Xuepu, demonstrating the high regard the financial authorities have for him. Chen, whose given name is Jian'an and hails from Zhuji, Zhejiang, came from a poor family. His father died early, and he was raised by his mother. Chen was intelligent from a young age, and especially studious once he began formal education. He was not discouraged by his family's poverty. Later, while studying at St. John's University in Shanghai, he caught the attention of Yan Zhuyun, the respected father of Yan Dunyuan, the former Minister of Interior of the Beijing government, who recognized his potential. At the time, Yan's fourth daughter, Shufen, was unmarried. Yan arranged for her to marry Chen. From then on, besides providing for Chen's educational expenses, Yan also occasionally provided him with money to send home to his family. After Chen graduated from St. John's, Yan further funded his studies in the United States, hoping for him to achieve advanced knowledge. However, while in the United States, Chen fell in love with a woman surnamed Cai and eventually married her. By the time he completed his studies and returned to China with his family, his household was established. His fiancee, Yan Shufen, then approached him, reprimanding him for forgetting the kindness of his benefactor and breaking his engagement. Chen initially prevaricated, but eventually broke off the engagement entirely. Shufen then filed a lawsuit for cohabitation against Chen in the First Special District District Court after Chen was appointed as the President of the Central Bank. She stated that she was already of advanced age (Shufen was in her thirties at the time), and if Chen insisted on not fulfilling the marriage agreement, she vowed never to marry again, requesting Chen to pay a certain amount of alimony to support her future life. The case was litigated for over a year, and the outcome was reportedly settled through mediation by relatives and friends of both parties. Last year, Yan Zhuyun's widowed daughter-in-law, Yan Zhumeizeng, initiated a lawsuit because Yan Zhuyun had left a will after his death mentioning that he had repeatedly lent money to Chen Xing in the past, amounting to a considerable sum of 25,000 yuan. Now that the relationship between Yan and Chen was no longer that of relatives, and Chen had risen in status and become wealthy, the old debt should be repaid. Yan Zhuyun's estate was inherited by his two grandsons, Yan Zhumeizeng's sons, Yongjie and Yongzhen. Yan Zhumeizeng, acting as their legal guardian, sued Chen Xing in the First Special District Court for the unpaid loan of 25,000 yuan and interest. However, the initial trial resulted in the plaintiff's defeat. Yan Zhumeizeng, unwilling to accept the outcome, hired lawyers Zhang Shizhao, Peng Yuanxun, Xue Dubi, Cao Shoulin, etc., to appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. In addition to citing Yan Zhuyun's will as evidence, they also included a letter from Chen's uncle, Chen Mianfu, to Ye Shuheng, regarding Yan's patronage of Chen: "Jian'an and you have been friends for many years and have received countless favors from the Yan family, almost nurtured and raised by them. If he has any conscience, how could he fail the Yan family and fail you?" This wording was intended to prove the authenticity of the loan, requesting the overturning of the original judgment and a favorable ruling. Yesterday afternoon, Presiding Judge Li of the Second Branch of the High Court convened a joint panel to hear the case. After the lawyer representing the appellant stated the grounds for the appeal, he added that in the spring of the 18th year of the Republic, the Yan family had even entrusted lawyer Jiang Baoli to write to Chen Xing demanding repayment. He noted that Yan Zhuyun had passed away in the summer of that year, and that part of the loan had been transferred through Ye Shuheng. All of this was supported by evidence. Even Chen's own letter to Yan Shufen mentioned "the Yan family's help with educational expenses." If he now denied it, it would be a contradiction of his own words. Chen Xing did not attend the hearing, but also hired a lawyer to represent him. However, his defense stated that the loan amount was only 1,300 yuan. After deliberation, Presiding Judge Li deemed it necessary to conduct further investigation and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

A Woman Accused of Fraud Had Two Gold Rice Bowls Customized

The Second Special Court Held a Hearing Yesterday and Requires Further Evidence Investigation Before Another Hearing

Cheng Xu, a local woman residing in a garret at No. 6 Dahua Lane, Bai'er Road, French Concession, age forty-four, had been continuously purchasing large quantities of gold jewelry and valuable jade ornaments from Lao Xiansheng Hengji Silver Shop since the beginning of October last year and then bringing them to exchange in the same shop. Zhao Lingzeng, a Ningbo native (age twenty-six) and the manager of the silver shop, regarded her as a great customer and eagerly welcomed her trades. The woman accumulated a debt of 5,201 yuan and 5 jiao 1 fen. Because she had no money to pay, she handed over twenty-nine pawn tickets for the jade ornaments as temporary collateral. On January 12th of this year, Ms. Xu suddenly gathered more than ten gangsters and went to Lao Baosheng Silver Shop, posing as detectives and claiming to be investigating stolen goods, and forcibly took the pawn tickets. At this point, manager Zhao Lingzeng realized that Ms. Xu was a swindler, and he hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the Criminal Division of the Second Special Court accusing Cheng Xu of fraud, along with a civil lawsuit. The court accepted the case and held a hearing, but the defendant was arrested by the Municipal Security Bureau for committing similar fraud cases in the Chinese Concession and transferred to the Procuratorate of the District Court for interrogation, so she could not appear in court. It was ordered to postpone the hearing. All the details have been recorded in previous reports. The Second Special Court prepared a document and dispatched police to the District Court to bring Cheng Xu to court. Yesterday morning, presiding judge Wu Fanglian held a hearing. First, the plaintiff's lawyer stated the intention to prosecute. Then, according to plaintiff Zhao Lingzeng, when the defendant came to purchase the goods, she claimed to be the mother-in-law of Kuang Zhongmou, the owner of the Penglai Market, and that compatriots of Kuang from Wuxi had entrusted her to purchase the goods in Shanghai. The total value of the transactions was around 18,000. Once, she came to buy two gold rice bowls, saying that Liu Hongsheng, a Ningbo gentleman in Shanghai, had asked her to buy them. Two days later, she handed over one of the bowls to Qinghua Silver Shop in Hongkou. Some of the goods were pawned at Baotai Pawnshop in Huangjiaguan. Around December last year, she said she had no money to pay, so she temporarily mortgaged the pawn tickets. Unexpectedly, on the 12th of this month, she sent people to come and forcibly take the pawn tickets. When she came to shop, everyone in my shop knew about it. When questioned, the defendant, Cheng Xu, replied, "Zhao asked me to sell the goods for him. He has hurt me so much that I can't stand it anymore. All the money for the goods I bought from him has been paid off, and I have invoices to prove it. Now, I only owe him about a thousand yuan." The defendant's defense lawyer then presented twenty-three invoices to the court. The court considered that the case still required the investigation of evidence and the summoning of witnesses, so it was ordered to wait for another hearing at a later date. The defendant, Cheng Xu, was remanded in custody.

Ferry Passengers Crowd After Double-Decker Pier Opens

Management Issues Notice to Inform Passengers

The Municipal Ferry Management Office's new double-decker floating pier built at the Bund on Beijing Road officially began operations yesterday. The original Tongren pier on Dama Road has been removed. The past two days have seen extreme crowding, with many spectators. To better facilitate passenger convenience, the Management Office has issued a notice. The original text is as follows: To improve passenger comfort and traffic management, this office has constructed a new double-decker floating pier on the Bund at Beijing Road. It includes ticket booths, waiting areas, tea rooms, reading rooms, car rental services, small shops, and business office, etc. Passengers will enter and exit on separate routes. The pier is comfortable and spacious, eliminating crowding. Passengers will no longer have to worry about wind and rain while waiting for the ferry. Porters have been hired to carry passengers' luggage, with set fees: ordinary items, 8 copper coins per piece; special items, such as those requiring two people to carry, 16 copper coins per piece. If there are any extra demands for payment, please report to the ticket seller at the pier or write to this office, and we will strictly punish the offenders. The pier construction has been completed, and all the long-distance and cross-river ferries that originally docked at Tongren Pier will be relocated to the new pier on Beijing Road starting on January 28th of this year. Fearing that this is not widely known, we issue this public notice.

During the Spring Festival Holiday, Why Not Visit Chao Mountain and Haiyun Cave?

The plum blossoms of Chao Mountain in Zhejiang and Hangzhou are the most beautiful in the Southeast. Recently, due to the warm weather, spring is coming early. The fragrance of the plum blossoms on Qunyu Mountain is gradually spreading. Haiyun Cave is the most beautiful place in the whole mountain. Not only does it offer a high vantage point, but the plum blossoms along the mountain for thirty li can be seen at a glance. The snowy blossoms resemble a sea, creating a grand spectacle. Moreover, the scenery is serene and secluded, no less so than the misty and rosy clouds on West Lake. Therefore, poets and artists have often visited this place and left inscriptions. The cliffs are covered with calligraphy. The late Wu Changshuo, a master of art, also carved his excellent poems here, which will last for a thousand years. The Qianyuan Temple next to the cave houses the tombstone of Ding Gong, written in regular script by a calligrapher during the Ming Dynasty, as well as clay sculptures by Liu Lan and stone carvings of Ming Dynasty officials Ding Xixuan and his son. These historical records can be seen here. Recently, the small paths leading into the mountain have been paved into a wide road. All the remaining historical sites have also been reorganized. The Taoist temple and guesthouse have been renovated. During the Spring Festival holiday, those who are tired of the hustle and bustle of the city, why not visit?

Fourth Sheet

The Kidnapping of Gao Maogong

Detained for Five Days and Nights, Bandits Give Travel Expenses and Force Him to Leave Shanghai

Gao Maogong, a 32-year-old engineer from Xinchang, Zhejiang, working at the Shunchang Iron Factory in Zhoujiaqiao, Bailinan Road, Zhabei, was mistakenly kidnapped on the morning of the 19th of this month. On the 23rd, Gao's wife, Shi Lanxuan, suddenly received a telegram from Gao in Xinchang, Ningbo, stating that he had escaped danger and arrived home. At that time, the city's police authorities, in order to clarify the truth, dispatched detectives by boat to Xinchang to investigate. All the details have been recorded in this newspaper. Detectives Zhu Bengui and Zhong Xuehuai returned to Shanghai yesterday after completing their mission and reported to the team. According to them, Gao was seized by the bandits, and they put dark glasses on him. Two bandits with guns guarded him on both sides. When the car stopped near the Mingxing Film Company on Dumei Road in the French Concession, the bandits took Gao out of the car and transferred him to a pre-arranged bandit car parked by the roadside. At that time, Gao's eyes had been covered with a black cloth by the bandits, so he could not tell the route or direction. He only felt that there were many turns. Soon the car stopped again, and he was pushed into a house and walked up to the third floor. Only then did his eyes see the light of day again. However, the 130 yuan in cash, business cards, and silver watch he had on him had been searched and taken away by the bandits. At the same time, the bandits also realized they had mistakenly kidnapped him, so after briefly asking about Gao's background, they handcuffed his hands, locked him in a room, and sent bandits to guard him in shifts day and night. For five days and nights, Gao constantly pleaded with the bandits, hoping for his freedom. Until the afternoon of the 23rd, a bandit went to deliver a message, claiming that "the commander (bandit leader)" had approved his release and gave him ten yuan for travel expenses, ordering a bandit to accompany him to the Ningshao Wharf in Nanshi, forcing him to board a Xin Beijing steamer to leave Shanghai, forbidding him to speak out along the way and not to look back, otherwise he would be harmed. Gao was forced to board the boat to Ningbo, and then sent a telegram to Shanghai to report the news. Gao is currently ill in his hometown, so he cannot come to Shanghai for the time being. The public document from the Xinchang Public Security Bureau and the details of the case have been reported by Wang Dasui, the chief of the Caojiadu branch, to the General Bureau for filing, and he has continued to order his subordinates to strictly arrest the criminals for investigation.

A Large Gambling Den Raided in Qichang Dock, Pudong, 25 People Arrested

Recently, someone set up a large-scale gambling den in house number 30, lane 223, Qichang Dock, Pudong, called Bagu Company, soliciting customers to gamble. There were many types of gambling, including shaking Bao dice, Pai Gow, poker, etc. The stakes were high. After the Pudong Public Security Bureau found out about it, Zhang, the chief of the branch bureau, dispatched servicemen Shao Ying, patrol police chief Guo Yongliang, and more than ten policemen, including Zhang Qiming and Liu Shaotang, to surround the gambling den at 12:40 a.m. the other day. They immediately went inside to search and arrested on the spot the gambling head, Wang Xianglang, from Chongming, and gamblers Wang Bizhong, Wang Yanglang, Chen Genfa, Lu Ruigong, Chen Zhaosheng, Wang Jinxiang, Wu Anqing, Yin Sheng, Xu Zhengfu, Xu Afu, Liang Wenbao, Jia Gengen, Li Shifa, Shen Bingzhang, Ge Weiming, Wu Jinfu, Zhao Sanlang, Zhang Heshang, Gu Xieqing, Yang Xiangkui, Shi Ada, Yu Mengchu, Xu Hongshi, and Yin Jiamei, a total of twenty-five men and women. They confiscated gambling equipment: one Bao box, one Pai Gow set, one poker set, twelve decks of playing cards, a stack of tally sheets, one money cylinder, gambling money: 16 yuan in silver dollars, 1 jiao 8 fen in small silver coins, and 30 copper coins. The witnesses were also taken to the bureau. Gambling head Wang Xianglang confessed that he had organized the gambling because of financial difficulties and had been taking a cut. The gamblers all made excuses. Bureau Chief Zhang, with the witnesses in custody, did not allow them to deny it and ordered them to be sent to the General Bureau for disposal yesterday morning.

The German Manager of a Mushroom Factory Indecently Assaulted a Young Girl

Yu Daqiao Was Victimized and the Prosecutor Investigated

Yu Hanqing, a native of Hubei, used to work as a messenger in the Songhu Garrison Headquarters. When the war broke out in Shanghai, Yu resigned and has been unemployed since then, living in Lincoln Road, Dada West Road, Shanghai West. Yu's wife, Ms. Mao (from Suqian), and their fourteen-year-old daughter, Daqiao, used to work in a yarn factory. Recently, Ms. Mao and her daughter switched to working at the nearby Daxi Farm (i.e., mushroom factory). However, after finishing work each day, Ms. Mao would return home first, while Yu Daqiao had to stay at the factory for one or two hours before returning home. This went on for about two weeks. Ms. Mao noticed that her beloved daughter was exhausted and very different from before, so she interrogated her. Eventually, she learned that the manager of the mushroom factory, a German named Xu Naiman (transliteration), had licked her lower part and threatened to keep it a secret. The woman was shocked to hear this. She believed that the Westerner had abused the young girl, violating human ethics and morals, and harming her beloved daughter's body. Therefore, she was unwilling to accept this and filed a lawsuit with the District Court, stating the facts. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wang Jianqing was ordered to escort the plaintiffs, Ms. Yu Mao and her daughter Yu Daqiao, to arrest the suspect. The police first reported to the Lincoln Road Police Station, and then secretly dispatched police officers to the factory to arrest the Westerner Xu Naiman and immediately brought him to the court. Prosecutor Zhang Zi conducted an investigation and ordered him to be detained for further investigation.

Special Document

Guidelines for Shanghai Municipal Facilities in the 24th Year of the Republic of China (Continued)

Mayor Wu's Report at the Expanded Commemoration Week

(II) Resolving the Rickshaw Problem: The rickshaw problem has become a significant issue in Shanghai today. All those concerned about social issues are racking their brains, diligently researching how to improve the rickshaw system and the lives of rickshaw pullers. Not only those concerned with social issues are conducting extensive research, but also foreigners in the Public Concession are earnestly studying it. Rickshaw pullers are Chinese, and their suffering should be deeply understood by us. They pull their rickshaws on the streets all day long, regardless of exhaustion or breathlessness, wind or rain, or under the scorching sun on asphalt roads that are almost melting and scalding their feet, continuing to run tirelessly. Some even work hard all day without earning enough for basic necessities. Therefore, many foreigners passing through Shanghai have said to me, "Why don't you improve the lives of rickshaw pullers who live like cattle and horses? Why don't you find a way to solve this problem?" Indeed, this is a social problem that urgently needs our attention and resolution. We know that, in reality, we cannot completely eliminate rickshaws, but we cannot ignore or fail to improve this system and the lives of rickshaw pullers. Therefore, this is also a responsibility that the Shanghai Municipal Government should strive to fulfill this year. I now have a suggestion to put forward for everyone to consider. I think the first step should be to pilot rickshaw puller cooperatives in the urban area. Initially, the rickshaws would be owned by the government, and gradually become jointly owned by the government and rickshaw pullers. Then, in the next step, they would become the sole property of the rickshaw pullers, achieving the goal of "rickshaw pullers owning their rickshaws." Our method and steps would roughly be as follows. This would not only improve the rickshaw system but also improve the treatment and lives of rickshaw pullers. In this way, the rickshaw problem might be solved. This is also work that our government should actually do for the people. I hope that all colleagues in the Municipal Government will study this together and ensure that it is implemented this year. This is the second thing that the Shanghai Municipal Government should strive for this year.

(III) Promoting Production Education: Regarding this issue, Director Pan and I have discussed it repeatedly over the past year and plan to implement it this year. It has been thirty or forty years since China began implementing modern education. The results of modern education over these three or four decades have not yet met our expectations. This is partly due to errors in our education system and spirit, and partly because the old ideas of the Chinese people have not yet been completely changed. This old idea is that scholars wear long gowns and use pens, while those who do not study wear short jackets and work in the fields. This has created a phenomenon where scholars do not engage in production, and those who engage in production do not study. This must be said to be the failure of promoting modern education over the past three or four decades. Therefore, six or seven years ago, when I was in Zhongshan County, I submitted a proposal to the Zhongshan County Political Training Committee. I wanted to completely reform the schools in each district of Zhongshan County. Except for the county-run higher primary school, all other schools would be converted into vocational schools. My intention was not only to enable everyone in the rural areas to know how to produce, but also to cultivate the backbone of talent in the rural areas to manage local autonomy. Currently, there are two dangerous symptoms in rural China. One is that children from rural areas who go to school do not engage in farming. Not only do they not engage in farming, but they also leave their hometowns and go to the county seat, and then from the county seat to the cities. Therefore, the result of the development of rural education is that the rural population decreases day by day, and the number of rural production elements also decreases day by day. Rural production naturally decreases accordingly, leading to the collapse of the rural economy. The second is that there is simply no one in the current rural areas who can manage autonomy. Those who engage in production in the rural areas are not educated, and those who are educated leave the rural areas to go to the cities. They neither engage in production nor serve their hometowns. In the past, there were local tyrants and evil gentry who managed local affairs. While local tyrants and evil gentry who exploited the villagers should be overthrown, there is no one to succeed them and manage local affairs and serve the local community. Not only is local autonomy impossible to implement, but the rural areas are also becoming increasingly empty. These two dangerous symptoms in rural areas are the biggest reasons for rural bankruptcy. To save the current symptoms of rural areas and avoid the collapse of rural areas, we must implement production education and reform the mistakes of past education to be successful. Therefore, this city plans to implement production education this year, opening a vocational middle school and dividing the suburbs of Shanghai into four districts: east, south, west, and north. Each district will add a vocational primary school centered on rural areas. Each primary school will have an attached farm, one for horticulture, one for fruit trees, one for rice cultivation, and one for animal husbandry. Colleagues, you must know that Shanghai is a large metropolis with three or four million people. The amount of agricultural products consumed in Shanghai every day is extremely large. Not to mention vegetables and fruits, the consumption of flowers alone, according to surveys and statistics, has reached a huge sum of ten thousand yuan per day. These large quantities of agricultural products are mostly supplied by the suburbs of Shanghai. However, the farmers in the suburbs of Shanghai do not plant in the right way, and the production of crops is not abundant, resulting in land being wasted, which is a pity. Therefore, we want to attach various farms to the vocational primary schools in the four districts of east, south, west, and north, so that the children of farmers in the four suburbs of Shanghai can receive not only general education but also various production knowledge and skills. Not only that, but it can also give middle-aged and elderly farmers in the rural areas an opportunity to increase their agricultural knowledge in order to improve agricultural production methods. In addition, we will also set up a relatively complete vocational middle school as a place for further study for the children of farmers. As for other schools, we also want to gradually improve them. This is the third thing that the Shanghai Municipal Government should strive for this year.

(IV) National Military Training: Everyone knows that military training in Shanghai is currently limited to schools and defense corps, and is mostly makeshift, or even nominal, failing to meet our expectations. Therefore, this year, regarding national military training, we want to come up with a new system and method, training in shifts and in a centralized manner. It is not enough to just train in schools or defense corps. We must train in a way that thoroughly disciplines, collectivizes, and militarizes the loose, chaotic, and dispirited lives of our general public, fundamentally refreshing the spirit of our nation and enriching the self-defense capabilities of our citizens. This is the fourth thing that the Shanghai Municipal Government should strive for this year.

(V) Popularizing Mass Education: Popularizing education is a fundamental task for developing national strength and promoting municipal administration. Currently, in Shanghai, we roughly estimate that among the three or four million citizens, about 25% of adults are illiterate, so-called illiterates. Now the central government has decided on a plan to popularize mass education. We now want to use one year to educate the adults in this city in order to solve the problem of illiteracy. The plan is to first find ways to teach the illiterate people in this city between the ages of fifteen and thirty to read this year, and then teach them the basic common sense that citizens should have, in order to establish a foundation for developing national strength and promoting municipal administration. This is the fifth thing that the Shanghai Municipal Government should strive for this year.

(VI) Repairing Embankments: The embankments of this city have been in disrepair for many years and are deteriorating day by day. Every year in July and August, Director Shen always asks for funds to repair them. Although the municipal government is in dire financial straits, it still allocates funds for repairs. However, because funds are limited, they are repaired and then damaged again, and to this day, we cannot help but consider it a hidden worry. Therefore, we want to greatly repair them this year if the municipal government's finances allow, raising one million yuan. Although we dare not say that it can be done once and for all, we must at least find a reasonable solution to the embankment problem in Shanghai. This is the sixth thing that the Shanghai Municipal Government should strive for this year.

The above six undertakings are all tasks that the colleagues of the Shanghai Municipal Government should work together on this year. Governance is not about talking too much, but about being consistent in word and deed, and being effective in action. What China needs most at this time is practical and rapid action. Empty talk is of no help in these difficult times. In the past, the facilities of this city, although constrained by financial and other factors, have not dared to be said to be fully satisfactory, but at least most of what was said has been put into practice. How are we going to make what has been stated today consistent in word and deed and effective in action? There are two prerequisite issues: one is the issue of how to raise funds, and the other is the issue of methods and plans. Although I have given these two issues deep thought and have some ideas, for the sake of gathering wisdom, I am now specifically proposing them again, asking all the colleagues of the entire municipal government to study and design them together. On the one hand, study how to raise funds, and on the other hand, design how to carry out the plan. Then, everyone will work together to make it so that all the comrades who serve in the Shanghai Municipal Government in the 24th year of the Republic of China will make a very significant and fruitful contribution to the society of Shanghai and the three or four million people of Shanghai this year, and not disappoint the good times of the 24th year of the Republic of China, as well as the ardent expectations of all the citizens for us.

Today's commemoration week coincides with the third anniversary of the January 28th Incident, so we have specially gathered colleagues from various bureaus here to jointly hold it, remembering the past and inspiring the future. Therefore, I will report the guidelines that the colleagues of the Shanghai Municipal Government should strive for this year to all comrades, and I hope that all colleagues will work together to ensure that these plans can be realized. Dr. Sun Yat-sen told us, "The purpose of revolution is construction, and the most important thing in construction is the people's livelihood." He also said, "The purpose of revolution lies in the implementation of the Principle of People's Livelihood. If the Principle of People's Livelihood is not implemented, there is no need for revolution." From this, we can see the importance of the people's livelihood. If the people's livelihood can be solved, our country can be rich, and the people can be strong. A rich country and strong people can enrich the strength of the country. After the strength of the country is enriched, it can guarantee the survival of our nation. A few days ago, when Chiang Kai-shek passed through Shanghai, he summoned the responsible comrades of this government. He told us that in the past few years, due to various reasons, our work has been biased towards the static aspect. This year, our work should be biased towards the dynamic aspect. The so-called dynamic work is to do more social construction work, and social construction work should pay more attention to the people's livelihood. Therefore, we have decided to use the six points just mentioned as the direction of our efforts for the Shanghai Municipal Government this year, and to use education, cultivation, and hygiene as the highest principles of our Shanghai Municipal Government's administration in the future. I sincerely hope to work with all the colleagues of this government to strive towards this goal and make achievements in the 24th year of the Republic of China. (End)

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Heaven

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 8: Remote Land, Weak Officials, Strong Orders from Afar; Grand Banquet in a Fine Hall, with Pitiable Creatures Outside

Zhang Jiefu had never heard of such a thing, and couldn't say a word for a long time. After a while, he said, "I really didn't expect that it would be so difficult to get an official position in Shaanxi." Zhiqian smiled and said, "In that case, Zhang, doesn't that diminish your interest in becoming an official?" Jiefu had finally managed to get Zhiqian to agree to help him, but now he suddenly said that the position was not worth taking, which was like cutting off his own path. So he smiled and said, "In my opinion, such counties must be in the minority. I don't think all the counties in Guanzhong are like that." Zhou Yourong smiled and said, "Everyone knows that, but if there's a good place, who wouldn't want to go? I'm just afraid that we, coming from so far away, will be seen by the authorities as being here to work, and they won't give us the easy positions." Zhang Jiefu lowered his head and thought for a moment. What he said made sense. However, what he wanted was just a minor position, and he certainly wouldn't come into direct conflict with the military authorities, so he didn't need to be completely discouraged. At that moment, he could only smile and say, "Well, it depends on human effort." Zhou Yourong smiled and said, "That's right. Although Shaanxi is a tough place, there are quite a few county magistrates who have gotten rich and gone home, so how did I get beaten back? If a gentleman like Zhang has that kind of spirit, and isn't afraid of being beaten, then maybe he can get an official position and make a fortune." Zhang Jiefu felt that his words were a bit aggressive, and his face reddened slightly. Zhou Yourong also realized that he had said something wrong, and quickly changed the subject, asking Zhiqian, "Brother Zhiqian said he was going to introduce some women for employment, what kind of women are they?" Zhiqian said, "Does County Magistrate Zhou need a maid?" Yourong waved his hands repeatedly, "No, no, I have a friend, whose wife has just arrived in Xi'an from the East, and she has two young children, making things very inconvenient. She must have a maid. And besides needing someone to do general chores, she also needs someone to lead the children." (125)

What I Saw in the Naked Country

— By Kang Jianzhaifu

| Short Fragments of Primitive Life |

Recently, a friend sent a letter from the South Pacific Islands. In his wanderings, he came to a little-known coral island not far from Australia. There, he saw tattooed barbarians with cropped hair and naked primitive people living in nests.

The people there, young and old, male and female, all wear nothing except for a cloth woven from banana leaves or bark to cover their private parts, and the rest of their bodies are naked all year round, bathing in the sunlight of nature. The young women's breasts are high and erect, the larger the more beautiful.

Because they don't wear clothes, both men and women consider tattoos to be beautiful. Children have their foreheads and noses tattooed from a young age. At the age of eleven or twelve, girls begin to wear skirts. This skirt is just a strip of banana leaf cloth to cover their private parts. At that time, from the waist to the knees, front and back, they are all tattooed with fish patterns. When they are about to give birth for the first time after marriage, they tattoo their breasts, chest, back, arms, and even their chins with flowers, leaving no gaps. When they are being tattooed, their skin breaks and bleeds, causing great pain. But in order to satisfy their aesthetic appearance, they

The Development of Shanghai Hospitals (Middle)

— Shanghai News Agency

At that time, there was also a hospital in the British and American concessions named "Tiren Hospital." In 1882, due to insufficient funds, it was merged into Tongren Hospital on August 14 of the same year.

In January 1887, Wu Hongyu again persuaded Li Qiuping, the Chinese manager of Gao Yi Foreign Firm, to donate 5,000 yuan, which was originally intended for the construction of the Jing'an Temple, to the hospital. He also raised the same amount from relatives and friends. As a result, Tongren Hospital was able to renovate suitable buildings, and its scale was further expanded.

In 1903, the women's department of Tongren Hospital was separated and established on Edinburgh Road, named Guangren Hospital.

(Note) This statement is based on "The Shanghai Handbook" by Pastor Davin De, but we believe that the so-called "Mai" should refer to Walter Henry Medhurst rather than Morrison. Medhurst arrived in Shanghai at the same time as Walter Henry Medhurst. The people of Shanghai certainly knew him better than Morrison. Moreover, is it necessary to misinterpret the sound of the character "Mai"? This is recorded for reference.

Subsequently, we will list the foreign public hospitals, the most famous of which are the General Hospital and the Paulun Hospital. The General Hospital is located by the Suzhou River and is easily seen looking north from the Garden Bridge (that is, the Outer Bund Bridge). It was founded in 1864 and rebuilt in 1920. Its organization is "a permanently elected board of directors according to their positions (including three consuls-general, four taxpayers from the Public Concession, and two taxpayers from the French Concession) to carry out its duties." The nursing duties of the hospital have always been undertaken by the Sisters of Charity of St. Vincent de Paul for 50 years without change. In 1912, due to difficulties in the French church and the fact that those in charge of the church believed that nursing hindered pure practice, the entire group resigned.

In 1899, the area around Xinzha was designated as the International Public Concession, and the Municipal Council of the former British and American Concession took over the merged management. The leading consul (the German Consul-General, Knappe) advocated building a hospital because the foreign population was dense and the poor and sick were pitiful. It was named "Tongji" so that it and Renji Hospital in the old British Concession and Tongren Hospital in the old American Concession stood together in a tripod-like manner. Because he was German, he advocated that it should be a German-style hospital, so he invited the famous German medical scientist Dr. Paulun to preside over the hospital, and also received a lot of help from Althoff, the German Chancellor, in terms of funding. The hospital opened in May 1902. In 1909, Dr. Paulun passed away, so Tongji Hospital changed its name to commemorate him.

The Public Concession Municipal Council also established several hospitals for special municipal needs, which were managed by the Health Department, namely:

Isolation Hospital Established in 1904

Mental Hospital Established in 1907

Chinese Police Hospital Established in 1907

Indian Police Hospital Established in 1908

Prison Hospital Established in 1903

From 1843 to 1903 (from the year Shanghai opened as a port to the year before the Russo-Japanese War), Shanghai's hospital business was almost entirely monopolized by foreigners. Even if Chinese people occasionally learned new medical skills, they only served in foreign hospitals. In the spring of 1904, the Russo-Japanese War broke out, affecting Northeast China. Shanghai people such as Shen Zhongli and Wang Peiyuan initiated the International Red Cross Society to rescue people in the war zone. After the war ended, it was renamed the Chinese Red Cross Society and successively opened three hospitals in Shanghai to provide daily services to the community:

(1) General Hospital Haig Road Established in 1910

(2) North Shanghai Hospital Xinzha Road Established in 1913

(3) South Shanghai Hospital Waitan Road Established in 1913

From August 1932, the names were changed, and in the order listed above, they were called "First," "Second," and "Third" Hospitals.

This was the beginning of Chinese-run hospitals. Then there were two more public hospitals known for their historical achievements:

Public Shanghai Hospital Established in 1909, gentry Li Zhongjue borrowed the Jicang public land to raise donations for construction.

Good Quality Products from Middle Schools, Normal Schools, and Vocational Schools

Too Few Agricultural and Farming Achievements

The products of vocational schools are practical and no different from actual commodities, and they can also use local specialty products to make practical items. Elementary schools can use labor teaching materials to make various national defense toys, arousing children's interest in national defense and paying attention to national rejuvenation. Schools pay little attention to investigating local production businesses, and many products do not seem to be the usual achievements of students but are made specifically for the exhibition.
